British Ambassador to Spain Has Been Recalled to London: British Government First to Implement UN Resolution; Spanish Newspaper Accuses British Ambassador of Transgressing

[Associated Press, London, 25th] British Ambassador to Spain, Sir Victor Mallet, has been recalled to his home country and arrived here by plane today. The United Nations General Assembly passed a resolution in New York, calling on member states to recall their ambassadors to Spain to express disapproval of the Franco government. Mallet is the first ambassador recalled by the United Nations.

[Reuters, Madrid, 26th] British Ambassador Mallet departed for his home country today. Madrid newspapers recently published news that made Mallet feel uneasy, alleging that the British Embassy here had actively participated in the anti-Franco movement. In fact, although the British Embassy here has had contact with various factions in Spain while engaging in customary social activities, as far as British reporters know, anti-Franco figures in Spain are still dissatisfied that the British and American embassies have not dared to actively sympathize with them. The internal relations of the various anti-Franco factions in Spain have not improved in the past year. When Britain, the United States, and France issued a declaration on March 4th, expressing their hope that the Franco government would voluntarily step down and establish a provisional government to hold general elections, the royalists among the anti-Franco factions were greatly angered. By July and August, negotiations on unified action among the various anti-Franco factions had almost completely stalled, and the factions still could not agree on the form of the future government of Spain. In September, the Communist Party abandoned cooperation with the various factions and decided to adopt resolute republicanism, further dividing the anti-Franco factions in Spain.

A Major Post-War Issue: Repatriation of Japanese Soldiers and Civilians

The three million people from the Chinese mainland have already been repatriated. In addition, there are still one million people who were originally in the Northeast. Due to the complexity of the national situation, the fate of these Japanese is still uncertain.

Repatriating millions of Japanese prisoners of war and expatriates from China to Japan is indeed a huge and difficult task, but with the cooperation of China and the United States, it can be said that it has been "successfully completed."

On the day the Japanese Emperor announced the unconditional surrender edict, the day the Japanese army laid down their weapons, was also the day the World War and the Sino-Japanese War officially ended. There were four million Japanese soldiers and expatriates in China, but after a year of efforts, three million of them have returned to their homeland. The remaining one million were originally in Manchuria (the Nine Northeastern Provinces). Due to the unfathomable Soviet policy, the repatriation of these one million people cannot be resolved for the time being, and the United States also feels powerless.

Larns, a special correspondent for "World Report Weekly," recently issued a report from Shanghai, explaining the details of the repatriation of Japanese soldiers and civilians very clearly. The main points are translated below.

The repatriation of Japanese soldiers and civilians began in December of last year with Sino-US cooperation. The method was to systematically disarm them first and gradually concentrate them. However, because China is vast and the Japanese soldiers and civilians are widely distributed, it had to be carried out in different regions. At that time, it was decided to deal with South China, Taiwan, and Vietnam first. In more than three months, a total of more than 600,000 Japanese were repatriated. The next was Central China, with a total of more than 800,000 Japanese repatriated. Finally, North China, with a total of about 554,000 Japanese repatriated, the latter of which was only recently completed.

When the repatriation work was underway, a noteworthy conclusion was reached regarding the extent to which Japanese expatriates had penetrated into China: the ratio of Japanese soldiers to expatriates was three to two. In other words, for every three Japanese soldiers repatriated, two civilians were repatriated. The progress of the repatriation of Japanese soldiers had a dual impact on Japan itself: on the one hand, there was a general sense of comfort, feeling that nationals scattered in various places had finally returned; on the other hand, it caused various economic worries.

On the positive side, many families were able to reunite, surplus manpower could be applied to production work, and the government would not be at a loss when drafting reconstruction plans. This raised the prestige of the United States a lot, because the United States, unlike the Soviet Union, was able to abide by the responsibilities stipulated in the Potsdam Declaration.

But on the negative side, the cost of repatriating Japanese soldiers and civilians had to be largely borne by the Japanese government, and this expense was considerable. At the same time, it was really a tricky thing to accommodate so many returning soldiers and civilians in Japan's fragmented economic structure after the war. What's more, the food and housing problems became even more serious. But no matter how bad the negative aspects were, the Japanese still felt that the rapid progress of the repatriation work was worthwhile. Therefore, no matter how huge the expenditure was, they still hoped to quickly send the one million Japanese soldiers and civilians in Manchuria back to their country. But this matter is more complicated because the Soviet Union is involved.

The rapid repatriation of Japanese soldiers and civilians from the US-controlled areas has made the Japanese feel dissatisfied with the Soviet measures. This can be seen from the recent demonstrations held by the Japanese in front of the Soviet Embassy in Tokyo, demanding the acceleration of the repatriation work. The Soviet Union has always paid close attention to Japan and has widely publicized the glory of communism and the Soviet Union's concern for the Japanese people, but the twists and turns of the repatriation work have obviously been a major blow to the work of the Japanese Communist Party and the Soviet delegation.

After many compromises, the Soviet Union finally decided to repatriate 10,000 to 15,000 Japanese people per month from a port in eastern Siberia (recent reports said that MacArthur and the Soviet authorities had established an agreement to repatriate 50,000 people per month—translator), but the Japanese still could not feel very satisfied, because the United States repatriated Japanese from mainland China, the peak of the work had reached as many as 12,000 people per day.

Another thing that made the Japanese dissatisfied was that the Soviet Union was preparing to send Japanese civilians first and delay the repatriation of Japanese prisoners of war as much as possible. According to various estimates, there are at least 800,000 Japanese soldiers in Soviet hands. The United States believes that 700,000 of them have been transported from Manchuria to Siberia to work in labor camps. The Japanese believe that this violates the Potsdam Declaration. At the same time, if the current method is followed, it will take at least several years to repatriate one million people.

Of course, no one can predict how future developments will unfold, because the situation may change at any time. But one thing is very noteworthy, that is, the repatriation of Japanese soldiers and civilians from mainland China has been completed. The war that Tokyo has always called the "Sino-Japanese Incident" has finally come to a formal end after a long nine years. (Translated by Ya Nong from "World Report Weekly")

Celebrating Christmas: British King's Broadcast Address; Encourages Nationals with the Word "Courage"

[Agence France-Presse, London, 25th] British King George VI spent Christmas today with the royal family at Sandringham House, sharing dinner together. Turkey and plum pudding were the main dishes. After the meal, the King entered the study and broadcasted a Christmas address to the nation in front of a gold microphone. Queen Mary, Queen Elizabeth, and princesses were all present to listen. The King encouraged the nation with the word "courage." His words were as follows: "Today, on Christmas Day, the Queen and I are gathered in the palace with the royal children, sharing this joyous occasion. We think of the British Empire as a large family spanning the globe. The war has left the world with scars and rubble everywhere. Politicians bear the heavy responsibility of stabilizing the world, and the past year has been a tireless effort, which is no easy task. Only by continuing to be patient and acting in good faith can the world return to normal. When Britain was bombed, we demonstrated our spirit, and in the future, we should still be able to show the same spirit with patience and discipline. Today, as free people, we celebrate Christmas in a peaceful environment. People still feel the lack of necessities in their daily lives, but we should not worry too much about the current difficulties, we should think of the great future. Mobilize the spirit of Christ to remedy our daily lives and relieve the suffering people everywhere."

[Associated Press, London, 25th] The Archbishop of Canterbury issued a Christmas message today, calling on people to increase their faith. He said that the situation is difficult, and the moral and physical conditions around the world are perilous, and everyone and everyone's spirit is oppressed by it. How can we still talk about increasing faith at this time? But Christmas tells us how to obtain peace and joy, and human beings cannot create peace and joy by themselves. Christ came to give peace and joy, and human beings must humbly accept it.

[Agence France-Presse, Tokyo, 26th] When Korean residents recently petitioned at Prime Minister Yoshida's official residence, they clashed with the police. Ten of them were arrested by the US military authorities, and the military court here opened trial this morning, charging them with "endangering the occupation policy."

On the trial stand of the Far East International Tribunal, the Presiding Judge rebukes the war criminals' lawyers for their quibbling (the one standing is Presiding Judge Sir William Webb, to his left are our Chinese Judge Dr. Mei Ru'ao and Soviet Judge General Zayanov)

US Denies Concluding Secret Treaty with Britain to Defend Against the Soviet Union

[United Press, Washington, 26th] Senior government officials recently issued a statement firmly denying rumors that the United States and Britain are preparing to conclude a secret defense pact against the Soviet Union. One senior official stated, "The United States has an obligation to abide by the provisions of the United Nations to take international defense measures, and has not concluded any secret or public agreement with any country."

France Dismantles Industrial Equipment in Occupied Areas of Germany: US Asks France to Explain Reasons

[Associated Press, Berlin, 26th] The US authorities formally requested the French side to explain the reasons for the alleged dismantling of industrial equipment by France in various parts of its occupied territory in Germany, transporting it to the Saar region, and setting up checkpoints around the Saar region.

American Christmas: Spending Billions

[Agence France-Presse, Washington, 26th] The Commerce Department announced today that the total expenditure of the American public on shopping and services in 1946 was $127 billion, of which $10.05 billion was spent on Christmas. This year's Christmas spending increased by $2 billion compared to last year, and by $3 billion compared to 1943.

International Female Devil: Venomous Old Beauty

[Agence France-Presse, Paris, 25th] Valley Dan, the captain of the Nice Mobile Reconnaissance Team, arrested a venomous beauty yesterday, suspected of killing more than twenty people. The arrested woman is Madame Tang Doulan, also known as the Baroness, and some even respect her as the Marchioness. She spent most of her fifty years in the Middle East, especially in Syria and Lebanon. In 1936, her husband, Baron Bell, was assassinated in a hotel in the Syrian desert, suffering nineteen stab wounds. The hotel was established by the Baron. Madame Tang sought revenge for her husband, resulting in the arrest of two suspects. However, two French military officers publicly suspected that the murderer was Madame Tang herself. Shortly thereafter, the two officers were almost run over by Madame Tang's car while out. The two reported to the police station, but to no avail. Later, Tang Doulan remarried a Muslim and lived in the home of a relative of the Arab king, in a state of virtual house arrest. In 1939, she secretly went to Mecca, the holy land of Islam, in order to sell a large quantity of jewelry and diamonds of unknown origin. She had previously seduced an official of a certain embassy, so she was able to leave the country smoothly. After arriving in Mecca, she plotted to kill an Arab chieftain, which angered the king, who sentenced her to death. However, she had great connections and escaped to North Africa. During World War II, she was even regarded as a political prisoner and given protection. This August, Tang Doulan came to Nice with her son (a reporter for a Nice newspaper) and began to enjoy life. Until recently, the mother and son were arrested for trafficking in gold, but her son was soon released. Reconnaissance Team Captain Valley Dan had followed her throughout Syria, Lebanon, and North Africa. According to him, "She is a most dangerous woman, she knows how to use poison or a dagger." It is said that fifteen to twenty men have died at her hands, but the police station is keeping the entire case a secret. Details will probably be released after the prisoner is escorted to Paris.

Three Planes Crash, Over Eighty Dead or Injured: All Flights Across Locations Suspended Yesterday; Bodies and Injured Sent to Funeral Homes and Hospitals Separately: Only One Child Passenger Uninjured, One Pilot has Hope of Survival

[This Newspaper] The aviation industry in this city experienced an unprecedented tragedy on Christmas Eve. China National Aviation Corporation flights No. 140 and No. 115, and Central Air Transport Corporation flight No. 48, flew from Chongqing to Shanghai. Upon reaching the airspace of this city, due to rain and heavy fog, they were unable to find a landing airport. After circling the airport for two to three hours, they ran out of fuel and crashed and burned one after another. China National Aviation Corporation flight No. 140 crashed near the runway of Longhua Airport. Flight No. 115 crashed near the No. 3 bridge on the Shanghai-Minhang Highway, next to the Hetamiao Temple on the Qiansan Road (from Qianliang Temple to Sanlintang). Central Air Transport Corporation flight No. 48 crashed in a rice field at the Zhangjiazhai residence in Jiangwan-Zhanghuabang. The three crashed planes had a total of eighty-two pilots and passengers (including five infants, not listed in the company's published list). As of last night, a total of sixty-six bodies had been transported to the Universal, China, and Central funeral homes. Fifteen injured people were sent to Zhongshan Hospital for treatment (of which Yu Peng died this morning). There is also a young child, who claims to be four years old named Wang Didi, who is the only survivor of this tragedy who was not injured at all. He is temporarily being fostered in the hospital as no one has claimed him.

Of the ten flight crew members of the three crashed planes, the only one with hope of survival is Preus, the American captain of China National Aviation Corporation flight No. 115. The company is doing everything possible to rescue him, hoping that he can escape danger.

As of last night, the statistics are: a total of sixty-seven dead, a total of fourteen injured, and one child safe and sound.

The China and Central companies dispatched personnel to the accident sites yesterday to clean up the remains. Due to the extremely bad weather yesterday, they telegraphed all locations to suspend flights. If the weather does not improve today, the suspension will continue.

Regarding the aftermath of this accident, the company stated that everything will be handled in accordance with government regulations.

(C) Flight crew members: Chen Ruirong (captain), Lou Lin'yi (co-pilot), Lin Dahua (radio operator), Qian Dingwu (trainee co-pilot). Secretary Wu said: All eleven of the above have died in the crashed aircraft near Zhangjiazhai, Jiangwan Airport. The bodies have been transported by car to the Central Funeral Home for viewing. As for the luggage and miscellaneous items on board, they have been scattered and lost at the accident site.

[This Newspaper, Nanjing, 26th] Those who boarded Central Air Transport Corporation flight No. 48 in Nanjing were Sun Ying, Mrs. Ni, and Zhu Xiangwu. Ni is the wife of the manager of the Wu Gong Hotel in Nanjing. Sun Ying is the goddaughter of the hostess of a certain dance hall in Shanghai. Zhu serves in the Ministry of National Defense and seems to be a colonel. Zhu was originally scheduled to fly to Shanghai on the 24th, scheduled to take off at 5:00 p.m. However, when he arrived at the airport, the plane had already taken off half an hour ago. The ticket was invalidated according to regulations, but later accommodated and changed to fly to Shanghai on the 25th, resulting in this disaster.

Complete List of Two China National Aviation Corporation Planes

Flight No. 48: Rushed Past Runway, Destroyed in Rice Field: Plane Body Caught Fire, No Survivors

The body and nose of Central Air Transport Corporation flight No. 48, which crashed in the rice field of Zhangjiazhai, Jiangwan-Zhanghuabang, were completely split and burned, with only the tail remaining. When reporters went to inspect the site yesterday afternoon along a muddy path, they still saw thick smoke rising from the remaining parts of the tail. In the rice field, there was a liver and lungs, purplish-red in color, and a severed female foot. Two people in military uniforms and a village child were groping in the rice field. One claimed to have found a gold ring, and the village child picked up several thousand-yuan and five-hundred-yuan banknotes, squatting in the rice field to wash away the mud.

The plane took off from Chongqing at 8:00 a.m. the day before and arrived in Shanghai airspace at 5:30 p.m. Due to the heavy fog, Longhua Airport did not have blind landing equipment, so it turned to Jiangwan. According to Central Air Transport Corporation, the plane made contact with the ground at that time, but due to the heavy fog and poor visibility, it rushed past the runway and crashed in the rice field, catching fire.

People Sitting Inside Their Homes, Disaster Comes from the Sky: Four Residents of Zhangjiazhai Killed or Injured

Two civilian houses in Zhangjiazhai were looted and destroyed, with the roof beams knocked several feet away. Although the two houses had been built for several years, the villagers nearby still called them "new houses." The householder, Zhang Guoye, works for the telegraph bureau and is currently in Nanjing. His wife, Zhang Qunxian, died on the spot. The villagers also call Zhang Qunxian "new bride," even though she has given birth to three children. Zhang Yuezhi, eleven years old, and Zhang Xinzhi, nine years old, were both seriously injured and have been sent to the hospital. Zhang Lindi, eight years old, was fortunate to only have scraped skin. Zhang Guoye's old mother, Zhang Lu, was also seriously injured and has been sent to the hospital.

A tiled house next to the destroyed houses was fortunately not affected. According to people in the house, around six o'clock the night before, they were having dinner when they heard two loud cracking sounds, followed by a deafening roar and a flash of light, as if a bomb had landed. The foundation of the house also shook. After the plane crashed, it caught fire and burned. They tried their best to put out the fire, but because the gasoline was burning fiercely, they could only move the straw on the side of the door and pour manure from the manure tank. At the same time, American troops stationed at Jiangwan Airport also rushed to help, and the fire was prevented from spreading, but the embers did not stop until dawn.

All eleven passengers and pilots and radio operators on the plane died.

Regarding the aftermath of the Central Air Transport Corporation flight No. 48 accident, Wu Lieqi, the secretary of the flight group, led many senior officials from the foreign affairs section, the general affairs section, and the vehicle allocation section to the accident site at 8:00 a.m. yesterday to transport the bodies of the victims to the China Funeral Home for injection and cleaning work. Soon, China National Aviation Corporation also sent the victims of the company's crashed plane to the China Funeral Home. As there were many bodies to be dealt with, Central was concerned that the funeral home would be too busy to cope, so after 7:00 p.m., the bodies were moved to the Central Funeral Home on Gordon Road, Mabai Road, and it was decided to perform the coffin sealing ceremony today. It is said that most of the victims have been identified by their families.

Remains of Central Air Transport Corporation Flight 48, which crashed in Huabang (Photo by Lu Shunxing of this newspaper)

Above: Bodies placed in the funeral home; Center: Pilot Preus, the only one with hope of survival; Below: Injured Chen A'er (Photo by Yu Chenshuo of this newspaper)

A Shocking Scene Beside Hetamiao Temple: Crash Site of Flight No. 115, Tragic Sight of Broken Planes and Dead People Everywhere: Corpses Mostly Ice-Cold from Night of Wind and Rain

China National Aviation Corporation's Chongqing-Shanghai flight No. 115 crashed in a pond to the right of Hetamiao Temple on Qiansan Road (from Qianliang Temple to Sanlintang) near the No. 3 bridge on the Shanghai-Minhang Highway. Reporters drove to the site yesterday morning in the wind and rain. After passing Shanghai Provincial Middle School to the south for several kilometers, there is a lane that can only accommodate a jeep, leading to Hetamiao Temple. The temple is close to the Huangpu River, four li away from the highway. From a distance in the car, one could see the silver-white wreckage of flight No. 115. Upon arriving in front of the temple, the first thing that caught the eye was an unbearable sight: twenty-nine bodies of deceased passengers, male and female, young and old, were lying in rows on the banks of the small stream in front of the temple. Among them were nine female corpses and three children's corpses. Their clothes were still intact, but having been subjected to a night of wind and rain, the corpses were all ice-cold. Five of them had their elbows bent upwards towards the sky, like statues. One corpse had its skull smashed and brains overflowing, another had a foot severed, and several had bloodstains on their faces, but most had no obvious injuries. According to nearby villagers, all the corpses were pulled from the small pond next to Hetamiao Temple, so some of the dead must have jumped out of the cabin when the plane was about to crash and drowned in the pond. It is also said that three people still had breath when they were rescued last night, but because it was midnight and transportation was inconvenient, there was no way to rescue them, so they soon died.

A Love Letter: The Person is Dead, But the Thing Remains

Flight No. 115 was destroyed in the small pond surrounding Hetamiao Temple. The nose of the plane was cut off, the right wing was broken, and the tail was split, but the body of the plane was still intact. Its landing state was completely like a normal stop. The western half of Hetamiao Temple was destroyed, with rubble everywhere. A mud statue of a "servant" in the temple had fallen to the ground, but the temple god in the main hall was still sitting unharmed. The open space behind the temple faces the wreckage of the plane. Fragments of documents and papers are scattered everywhere on the ground. At the cut-off point of the nose of the plane, business cards and blank checks toothpicks and other items were found. The reporter also picked up a "love letter" stained with mud. The date was the 23rd of this month, probably written by a female passenger on the plane but not sent. It read, "Dear ××, the date of departure still cannot be determined, I am really anxious... Yours, ××." Reading it makes one feel heartbroken. Broken clothes are still hanging on the branches of trees in the open space. The remaining clothes and other items in the plane are being cleaned up and piled on the lawn in front of the temple by personnel from China National Aviation Corporation.

Above: China National Aviation Corporation Flight No. 115, which crashed in the pond at Hetamiao Temple. Below: Corpses lying everywhere near Hetamiao Temple (Photo by Yu Chuangshuo of this newspaper)

A Loud Crash, Firelight Illuminating the Sky: Elementary School Principal Escapes Death

Although Hetamiao Temple was badly damaged, fortunately there were no casualties. However, Sun Jianjin, the principal of the private Huadong Elementary School in the village, escaped death. Principal Sun stays in the western part of the main hall of the temple every night. Around eight o'clock the night before, he was fast asleep when he suddenly heard a loud crash and woke up from his dream. At that time, the bed curtains had fallen down, and he felt that his feet were being pressed down by a heavy object. In a hurry, he poked his head out and saw firelight illuminating the sky. At that time, he never thought that a plane had crashed, but thought it was a fire caused by lightning, so he hurriedly got out of bed, put on his clothes, and fled. At this time, he was panicked and confused, and the east hall had been destroyed, so he could not identify the direction. Later, he calmed down a little and went around the bamboo garden behind the temple to the neighboring house, where he joined the villagers in ringing gongs to rescue. Principal Sun told reporters yesterday about the situation at the time, and smiled and said, "Fortunately, I have always slept with my head to the east and my feet to the west, otherwise my head would have been crushed and I would have died."

Drizzling Rain on the Road: Pedestrians' Souls Ready to Break

While the reporters were inspecting the surrounding area, two family members (male) of the victims came to identify the bodies. Obviously, the relatives they were looking for were among the corpses, so they were filled with tears. The county government had also sent people to handle the matter, but by the time the reporters left (2:00 p.m.), the bodies had not yet been moved. At this time, two cars were parked on the side of the road, and a woman in the car was looking around with tearful eyes. Seeing the reporters, she opened the car door and stood in the rain to inquire. She said that she was the wife of Le Zuolin, the general manager of Qinghua Paint Company. Her husband had called to say that he was taking China National Aviation Corporation flight No. 115 to Shanghai. This morning, after learning about the plane crash, she had inquired at various hospitals but had not found him, and feared that he had died. While speaking, she burst into tears.

Also, the personnel from China National Aviation Corporation who were taking care of the scene yesterday prohibited reporters from taking pictures of the corpses. One foreign staff even held an iron rod and tried to rush towards a photographer from a certain newspaper, which aroused public outrage and almost caused trouble.

Fifteen People Receiving Treatment in Zhongshan Hospital: Yu Peng Has Died of His Injuries: Zhang Chunhua and Xue Jinfan Least Injured

[This Newspaper] At 3:30 p.m. yesterday, Dr. Hoey (C.F. Hoey), the medical director of China National Aviation Corporation, went to Zhongshan Hospital to visit the injured passengers rescued from the two crashed planes of the company. China National Aviation Corporation sent three batches of injured people after the accident the night before, a total of fifteen people. The first batch of seven people: Yu Peng (seriously injured), Zhao Jixing (male), kidney laceration, bloody urine, skull fracture, unconscious. Liu Tengxiang (male), concussion. Chen A'er (male), right leg broken. Zhang Qiyun (female), injured head and left leg. Min Wanzhen (female), injured head and knees. Unnamed (female), has been unconscious since being sent to the hospital. The second batch of four people: Zhang Chunhua (male), fractured tibia and fibula of the left foot. Wu Rongbing (male), fractured ulna of the left hand. Xue Jinfan (male), injured arm, relatively minor. Preus (male, the captain of flight No. 115), seriously injured head and face, unconscious. Two unnamed children, one died at 6:50 p.m. yesterday, less than one year old. The other had two legs broken, about one year old. The third batch of two people: Wang Xiaode (male, the radio operator of flight No. 115), dislocated knee joint, four fractures of the femur, tibia, and fibula, brain laceration, in critical condition. Xu Weilong (male), injured head and face.

Among the aforementioned fifteen injured, Yu Peng died of his injuries yesterday morning. The unnamed female and Wang Xiaode extended until last night. Also due to serious injuries, they have entered a dying state. The rest are still in good condition. Among them, Zhang Chunhua and Xue Jinfan, passengers on flight No. 115, were the least injured. They were even allowed by the doctor to have a brief conversation with reporters.

Zhang Chunhua is a Beijing opera actor who sings the role of a male clown. Only his right ear and left heel were slightly injured. He is currently in a second-class ward on the second floor. At that time, a female friend named Zhou was comforting him. Zhang performed on the same stage as Li Shaochun at the Hankou Grand Theater, until the 16th when his contract expired. He could have returned to Shanghai with Li at the same time, but the theater had not yet paid Zhang the agreed fee, so he was delayed until the 25th before he could set off. He originally planned to rest in Shanghai for a while before immediately going to Tianjin to perform, but unexpectedly encountered the accident.

According to Zhang, the plane arrived in Shanghai airspace around 7:00 p.m. He was asleep at the time. When he woke up in extreme impact, the plane had already crashed. Zhang woke up from a coma and didn't even know he was injured. When he tried to stand up, he realized that his left leg was broken, and he rolled around next to the plane. It was not until after midnight that someone came to rescue him.

Xue Jinfan is a department store merchant who came to Shanghai from Chongqing to purchase goods. He had six partners traveling with him, and only Xue survived. Xue was sitting in the middle of the plane and only knew that it was impossible to land, and did not expect anything else. When the plane suddenly fell at the end, he lost consciousness. When he woke up, he saw that he had been thrown out of the plane and was lying on the river beach. Next to him was a woman, Xue himself had the ability to help each other, Shang Tu went forward to help, but unexpectedly it was a dead body. It was then that he realized that he himself had been injured and fell to the ground exhausted. After being rescued to the hospital, his condition was very good, and his relatives and friends had visited him many times.

The American pilot of flight No. 115, Preus, was seriously injured. When Dr. Hoey of China National Aviation Corporation entered the room to visit him, he was still unable to speak. His head, cheeks, and other places were all wrapped in gauze and silk ribbons. His left leg was fractured. Dr. Hoey instructed the doctors in the hospital to move Preus to the best ward, hire a special nurse, continuously transfuse blood when necessary, and use X-rays to check for internal injuries in the chest and abdomen. He also said: There is no problem with medical expenses, everything will be paid by China National Aviation Corporation. If Preus can be rescued, he will probably be the only pilot saved from the three crashed passenger planes.

Merchant Xue Jinfan with minor injuries; Miss Zhou visits Zhang Chunhua, the male clown (Photo by this newspaper)

China Airlines Announces Cause of Accident: Attempted Blind Landing Resulted in Crash, Total of Sixty Passengers on Both Aircraft

China Airlines issued the following public announcement yesterday regarding the cause of the recent accident:

It is with deep sorrow that China Airlines announces the loss of two passenger planes flying from Chongqing to Shanghai on the evening of December 25th. Aircraft No. 140, a C-47 model, piloted by J.M. Greenwood, co-piloted by Liu Linsen, and accompanied by radio operator Jin Keng, took off from Chongqing's Shanhu Ba Airport at 10:15 AM, with scheduled stops in Wuchang and Nanjing. Aircraft No. 115, a C-46 model, piloted by R.B. Preus, co-piloted by Tan Xingzheng, and accompanied by radio operator Wang Xiaode, took off from Chongqing's Baishi Yi Airport at 10:30 AM, with a scheduled stop in Wuchang before flying directly to Shanghai. Both planes departed Wuchang in close succession, fifteen minutes apart, with

the weather in both Nanjing and Shanghai being suitable for landing at that time. However, as they approached Nanjing, the weather in both cities suddenly deteriorated. Since Wuchang Airport lacked night-flying equipment, it was impossible to return. Both Nanjing and Shanghai airports were equipped for night landings, with Jiangwan Airport possessing more advanced blind-landing and night-flying capabilities. Aircraft No. 140, originally scheduled to stop in Nanjing, attempted to land there, but due to the weather, the airport was completely obscured. The pilot then continued to Shanghai. Aircraft No. 115 arrived over Shanghai at 5:30 PM, followed by Aircraft No. 140 an hour later. At that time, the weather in Shanghai was similar to Nanjing.

Aircraft No. 140 first attempted to land at Jiangwan Airport using the blind-landing equipment. The pilot circled over the area for over an hour, repeatedly attempting to land. However, due to a malfunction in some of the plane's radio equipment, it was impossible to utilize the blind-landing system. Although communication with the control tower was possible, the signal was too weak to establish contact with the blind-landing equipment. After attempting for another hour, it was determined that landing at Jiangwan was impossible, leaving no alternative but to proceed to Longhua. Upon attempting to land at Longhua Airport, visibility remained at zero. After several attempts, the pilot finally notified the control tower that the plane was out of fuel and had to make a forced landing. During the landing attempt, while correcting the landing direction, the plane crashed at the southwest end of the airport at 7:55 PM. As for

Aircraft No. 115, it circled over Jiangwan Airport and was able to establish contact with the blind-landing equipment, although the signal was sometimes unclear. Under such circumstances, a safe landing was also unlikely. At approximately 9:00 PM, it flew from Jiangwan to Longhua Airport. The weather had slightly improved by this time, and visibility gradually increased. After repeated landing attempts, the final attempt was nearly successful, requiring only one more circuit to change direction. Unexpectedly, at this precise moment, the plane crashed one mile southwest of the airport at the Huangjia Du River Temple Pagoda. The cause of the crash remains unclear. Aircraft No. 115 circled over Jiangwan Airport for three and a half hours. For the first two hours, Aircraft No. 140 and another China Airlines plane were also in the air.

Aircraft No. 147

In addition, two other aircraft, China Airlines Aircraft No. 147, landed safely at Jiangwan Airport at 7:40 PM. While Aircraft No. 140 was attempting to land at Longhua, China Airlines executives and aeronautical personnel were present at the airport, along with the airport's fire brigade, ambulances, medical personnel, etc., all on standby. The municipal police department and fire brigade were also notified and dispatched to the scene in case of emergency, allowing for timely rescue efforts after the accident. As for Aircraft No. 115, news of its accident was received approximately one hour after contact was lost. The U.S. military and U.S. Navy assisted in the search, with numerous boats dispatched by the water police and the U.S. Navy.

Reconnaissance Along the River

Aircraft No. 140 carried 27 passengers and 3 crew members. Aircraft No. 115 carried 33 passengers and 3 crew members. The injured have all been taken to hospitals. Unfortunately, the number of fatalities is quite high. The names of the passengers and other detailed information will be disclosed after further investigation.

Newlywed Couple Die Together; Wife of National Assembly Representative Dies as Well

In the International Funeral Parlor, the deceased lay quietly, many bodies already covered in flowers. The situation was different in the Chinese Funeral Parlor. Piles of corpses were stacked together, with blood, mud, and rainwater staining their clothes beyond recognition. The grief-stricken families could sometimes only identify their relatives by a single high-heeled shoe! The sound of weeping shook the ground; it was a tragic sight.

Xia Changjun, a victim of the China Airlines crash and a grain specialist from Shao, and his wife, Xia Wu Shuzhen, died together. Xia Changjun's death was particularly gruesome, with one leg severed. Yang Xizhi, the former Special Commissioner of Grain Administration, personally identified the body yesterday. Xia's wife's relatives fainted in grief upon seeing the remains! The Xia couple had only been married in May of this year, and unexpectedly became ill-fated lovers in less than a year! Liu Linsen, the co-pilot of the China Airlines plane, also perished in the accident, and he had only been engaged for two months. Yesterday, Liu's fiancée went to identify the body, and the scene was even more heart-wrenching!

Mrs. Zhao, the mother of a National Assembly representative from Liaoning, Shenyang, also known as Zhao Wang Yuxian, along with her son Zhao Jixing, boarded a plane from Chongqing to Beijing to visit the representative. Due to weather changes, the flight was diverted to Shanghai, and they unexpectedly met with disaster, mother and son dying together. Zhao's second son, Zhongxing, has arrived at the International Funeral Parlor to identify the bodies and arrange for the funeral. He has also urgently telegraphed Representative Zhao in Nanjing to come to Shanghai.

At the International Funeral Parlor, someone recognized a deceased person as their relative, Zhang Qiyun. However, Zhang Qiyun was resting peacefully in bed number 30 in room number 6 of Zhongshan Hospital. She was still able to speak, and she confirmed that she was indeed Zhang Qiyun. It was later discovered that there had been a misunderstanding.

The U.S. military police, or MPs, were driving quickly through the wind and rain in a Jeep to transport the injured to the hospital the night before. Unfortunately, the vehicle was traveling too fast and struck a pedestrian, Li Chen, injuring her head. As a result, she was sent to Zhongshan Hospital along with the crash victims.

At Zhongshan Hospital, two airplane tickets were found near the body of one of the victims. One ticket was in the name of Yu Peng, and the other was in the name of Zhang Zhenjiang, making it impossible to determine the deceased’s identity.

Next to the wreckage of China Airlines Aircraft No. 115, rescuers found a little boy wearing a floral cloth coat. Thank goodness, he was completely uninjured! When reporters arrived at Zhongshan Hospital, he had already been safely taken to the hospital and was asleep. He said his name was Wang Didi and that he was four years old. Who his parents are and where he came from are currently unknown. On the eve of Christmas, he may have been a beloved and happy little angel - but now he has become a wandering orphan!

Wang Didi, a Survivor, Is Surprisingly Safe and Sound

Ministry of Communications Dispatches Personnel to Shanghai to Console Bereaved Families and Supervise Safety Measures by Both Companies

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 26th] The Ministry of Communications is paying close attention to the accident and has dispatched Li Bohou, Director of the Navigation Administration Department, and Dai Anguo, Director of the Civil Aviation Department, to Shanghai as quickly as possible to comfort the injured passengers and the bereaved families, and to supervise the two airline companies in taking emergency safety measures. With the winter season of ice and fog upon us, all flights will be suspended in adverse weather conditions with poor visibility to ensure safety.

Aircraft No. 140 Crashed, Damaging Another Parked Aircraft

China Airlines flight from Chongqing to Shanghai, number 140, crashed near the main runway of Longhua Airport. The wreckage was cleared yesterday morning by the company using a crane. The No. 6 Red Cross ambulance, which overturned near the runway in the darkness while rescuing the injured and dead the night before, was also towed away. Scattered pieces of the aircraft can still be seen on the lawn at the crash site, along with a pile of torn clothing and shoes, blurred with blood stains. Some of the passengers were carrying Guang oranges from Sichuan, which now share the same tragic fate as their owners. Orange peels are scattered everywhere and have not yet been cleaned up.

On the night of the plane crash, the aircraft circled over the city for two to three hours. Finally, when the fuel ran out, the nose of the plane plunged directly to the ground, hitting the wing of another parked aircraft upon landing. The aircraft itself then flipped over several times and was destroyed.

While the two aircraft were circling over the city, Wu Shi, head of the company's aeronautical engineering group, McDonald, the chief pilot, Gao Dajing, head of the business group, Wu Zhihong, manager of the Shanghai ticket office, and American director Schweitzer, along with experienced pilots, were all waiting at the airport. Chief pilot McDonald personally directed operations from the control tower. Shen Desie, General Manager of the company, Mr. Lai Nuo, representative of Pan American Airlines, and Dr. Salade also arrived one after another to supervise the rescue efforts, continuing until the next morning without rest.

President Song Summoned Responsible Persons of Cotton Textile Industry Yesterday; Discussed Measures to Suppress the Rising Price of Yarn and Cloth; Stopped Rationing of Reproduced Cotton Yarn for Market Stabilization; Requested Purchase of Raw Cotton with Foreign Exchange, Half of the Finished Products Should Be Allocated to the Management Committee

President of the Executive Yuan, Song Ziwen, went to the Bank of China building at 9:00 AM yesterday to handle official business. At 10:00 AM, Mayor Wu Guozhen and important responsible persons from the Sixth District Machinery and Cotton Textile Industry Association, including Wang Qiyu, Rong Hongyuan, Guo Dihuo, and Tang Xinghai, paid a joint visit. Song received them and held a meeting for one hour, the content of which focused on suppressing the rising price of yarn and cloth, and deciding on issues such as increasing production. The principles can be divided into: (1) Stop rationing of reproduced cotton yarn and allocate the original quantity to the Spinning Management Committee for market stabilization at any time. (2) Private factories request foreign exchange to import raw cotton. After the finished products are produced, half of them should be allocated to the Management Committee for sales to the market to suppress the rising market price, and a part of it should be exported to exchange for foreign exchange. Regarding this method, the Spinning Management Committee should first draft a plan, set up a small group meeting to review it, and then submit it to the general meeting for approval, and it will be implemented on a trial basis starting from January next year. (3) It is hoped that private factories will promote the sale of domestic cotton as much as possible to save foreign exchange. Subsequently, Lin Fengbao of the Central Bank also reported to Song in detail that the Central Bank's sale of gold in Japan had been effective. At 12:00 PM, Song also met with Zhao Dihua, Xu Weiming, Hu Huichun and others from the financial community for discussions. At that time, Song also invited Xu Weiming to have lunch together. At 2:00 PM, he returned to write. After 4:00 PM, Song summoned Shu Yunchang of the Textile Construction Company and Yang Xiren of the Spinning Management Committee. At 6:00 PM, he also met with Xu Jizhuang, Director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, for discussions.

Calculations of Some House Donations and Construction Donations Have Problems; The Financial Committee of the Council Resolved to Request the Municipal Government to Reply

[Our reporter] The Financial Committee of the Municipal Council held its sixth meeting at the Hongqiao Club yesterday afternoon to continue discussing tax revenue and other issues. Hu Wenyuan, Deputy Director of the Finance Bureau, attended to explain. The matters discussed at the meeting: (1) Regarding the Finance Bureau's "Implementation Measures for the Collection of Food in Kind and the Discount of the Food Tax in 1935" and the "Provisional Measures for the Collection of the Food Tax and the Temporary Verification of the Grain Registry," the councilors Lu Shidao and Wang Weiyin were recommended to review them. The review opinions were submitted to the municipal government for reference. According to Deputy Director Hu's explanation: The city's food tax grain registry has always been in the hands of clerks (also known as "land skin ghosts"). Currently, the bureau is assigning personnel to verify according to the above-mentioned method. Since its implementation, the results have been very good, and there has been no harassment. The large-scale collection of the food tax can begin in February next spring.

(2) Citizens, the Chamber of Commerce, and alternate councilors have all proposed to the Municipal Council that the Finance Bureau's collection of the autumn house donation and municipal construction donation in this city is not calculated based on the rental value in the 26th year of the former Public Works Bureau. They requested that it be corrected. The committee decided to send these opinions to the municipal government for reply. Deputy Director Hu also explained: The Slaughter Tax Law, the Feast and Entertainment Tax Law, and the House Donation Regulations have all been amended by the national government, and there are many differences from the current system. Based on the city's collection experience, the Finance Bureau feels that there are some aspects that are not completely suitable for the local situation. It has repeatedly explained the reasons and telegraphed the central government for further amendments. This time, it is also prepared to submit it to the second general meeting of the Municipal Council for research. If the new tax law is implemented, it is estimated that the city's tax revenue will decrease by 3 billion yuan per month. Recently, the Executive Yuan ordered that local governments can levy three types of special taxes, but they must be approved by the public opinion organs. The municipal construction donation and the travel lodge donation in 1936 are still planned to be included in the budget, based on this order.

(3) Regarding the urgent request of the city's ballroom industry association to exempt the ballroom beverage tax and the request of the instrument and stationery industry association to exempt the business tax, it was decided to invite Finance to respond.

(4) The association also approved the telegram from the Qingdao Municipal Council, unanimously advocating that all land business tax revenue should be allocated to the local government. In addition, the property rental income tax, property sale income tax, and stamp tax should still be allocated by the central government, and the allocated percentage should be increased to 50% of the net income. It was decided to recommend that the second general meeting discuss and decide.

The Port Affairs Committee; The Anti-Smuggling and Guard Group; Cracked a Major Theft Case on the American Ship; The Stevedores Colluded with the Lighter Captain to Steal Goods; The Goods Were Hidden in Flour Bags and Valued at More Than Ten Million

[Our reporter] On the 22nd of this month, the anti-smuggling and guard group of the Shanghai Port Affairs Committee seized relief supplies and general commercial loans stolen from the American ship "Staghound," which was berthed at the Kailuan Wharf in the Rihui Port. The stevedores of the ship colluded with "Boss" Gong Shanqi of the lighter No. 787 of the Hsingchung Transportation and Storage Bureau to steal cargo and hide it on the lighter. The stolen goods seized included two large bundles of thin wool and dark blue serge, two woolen blankets, and two pounds of worsted yarn, tightly packed in flour bags, estimated to be worth more than ten million yuan. Hu Cai, who was on watch, and Yuan Yinfu, the cook, were also arrested on the spot. According to their confession, the goods transported by the vessel were indeed stolen by "Boss" Gong Shanqi of the vessel. The main criminal and the stevedores who participated in the theft have fled upon hearing the news. Hu Cai and Yuan Yinfu have been transferred to the police station for further interrogation. Their confession records have been submitted to Wu Guozhen, Director of the Port Affairs Committee, for review. The main criminal, Long Shanqi, has been notified by the group to the Hsingchung Transportation and Storage Bureau to pursue the arrest with bail, in order to bring him to justice. It remains to be determined whether the stolen goods were stolen or smuggled, and will be dealt with after investigation. This incident was secretly reported by Dong Huisai, Acting Supervisor of the 12th District, and Ding Baozhong, Assistant Supervisor. The Port Affairs Committee has issued a commendation order to encourage them.

Post Office Booth Established in North Railway Station Lobby

Post Office News: To facilitate passengers sending letters and expedite postal efficiency between Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou, the Shanghai Post Office has reached an agreement with the two Railway Administrations to establish a post office booth in the lobby of the North Railway Station. This booth will sell stamps and handle ordinary, registered, express, and airmail. The office hours are fixed from 7:00 AM to 11:00 PM. If the public has urgent letters after the business hours of other post offices, they can go directly to this booth to post them before 11:00 PM. The booth was established on the 27th of this month. As the designated location in the North Station lobby is still under renovation, it is temporarily operating in conjunction with the China Travel Service in the North Station.

Unimpeded Flow of Mail to the United States

According to China National Aviation Corporation news, airmail sent from Shanghai to the United States via the Philippines was previously transported to Manila by the company's China-Philippines flights and then transferred to Pan American Airways' Pacific route flights to the US. However, due to Pan American's flight suspension starting October 3, and because Pan American was the only airline contracted with the Philippine Post Office to transport mail to the US, the mail arriving in the Philippines was slightly delayed. Now, China National Aviation Corporation has received notification from Pan American's office in the Philippines that, starting November 5, all mail arriving in the Philippines will be transferred by the Philippine Post Office to US Air Transport Command (ATC) aircraft for transport to the US. Once Pan American flights resume, the mail will be transferred back to Pan American. From now on, mail to the US will flow unimpeded.

Unfinished Business of the Housing Allocation Committee: Municipal Government Takes Over and Is Nearing Completion

[Reported by this newspaper] After the Executive Yuan Housing Allocation and Management Committee concluded its work in mid-October, its unfinished business was taken over by the General Affairs Office of the Municipal Government. A reporter visited the person in charge of the office yesterday afternoon to inquire about the work progress in the past two months. According to him, the office handles housing allocation matters in accordance with the instructions of Mayor Wu as a principle: (1) No more housing will be allocated, and no more residence permits will be issued. (2) Investigate and handle disputes regarding houses allocated by the Housing Allocation Committee. (3) If it is discovered that the former Housing Allocation Committee issued residence permits in error, it will be ordered to revoke them.

It is reported that the office has discovered more than ten cases of erroneously issued permits, most of which involve people who moved in before April 20 of this year, before the Housing Allocation Committee was established, and who have legal leases with the owners. According to the scope of housing allocation by the Executive Yuan Housing Allocation Committee, it is limited to civilian houses formerly occupied by the Japanese enemy, totaling about six or seven thousand buildings. One or two thousand buildings were allocated to various agencies by the Housing Allocation Committee. The unfinished business has largely been completed. Therefore, the Municipal Government's General Affairs Office's part in taking over the housing allocation will also be announced as completed in January of next year. The office also issued a special announcement yesterday that residents who have been allocated housing by the former Executive Yuan Shanghai Agencies Allocation Committee can quickly negotiate leases with the owners using the temporary permits issued by the committee. If the owner refuses to sign a contract, they can request the Central Trust Bureau Real Estate Department to act as a unified tenant by the end of this year.

Communicating the Suzhou Creek: Plans to Add Bridges in Various Locations to Facilitate Transportation on Both Banks

[Reported by this newspaper] The Puxi area of this city is bisected by the Suzhou Creek, forming the areas north and south of the creek. There are more bridges east of Xizang Road, so north-south traffic is relatively convenient, and the Hongkou area is more prosperous. West of Xizang Road, there is only the Xinzha Bridge, which can cross the creek, so the Zhabei area is very deserted. Moreover, those traveling from Zhabei to Huxi and Nanshi mostly cross the creek along the bridges in the eastern district, which increases the traffic burden on the Huangpu district. The current congestion of vehicles on Nanjing Road and Middle Zheng Road is also partly due to this.

Zhao Zukang, director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, recognizing this, has drafted a transportation plan for both banks of the Suzhou Creek, preparing to implement it gradually. Yesterday afternoon, he went to conduct on-site inspections with Lu Jifang, director of the Road Department, and Zhu Guoxi, director of the Structural Department of the bureau, and closely studied the bureau's near-term plan to communicate the transportation engineering plan for the north and south banks of the Suzhou Creek. It is reported that the plan includes adding bridges at Jiangxi Road, Hengfeng Road, Fujian Road, and Changshou Road, and addressing the bridge site issues, repairing the entire surface of Suzhou Road and the revetment, and organizing and widening the main roads such as Jiangxi Road, Chengdu Road, Huasheng Road, Hengfeng Road, Middle Zheng North Second Road, Changchou Road, and Guangzhao Road. The total planned amount is more than 9 billion yuan, which will soon be submitted to the Municipal Council for deliberation. After the completion of this plan, the benefit to the eight or nine thousand acres of land in the Zhabei area, considering only the increase in land value, would be at least 40 to 50 billion yuan, and the vehicle congestion in the Huangpu district would be greatly alleviated.

Delay in Import of Sea Vessels: Wusongkou Merchant Ship Suffers Damage to Bottom of Hold, Dahua Ship Rescheduled to Sail to Ningbo This Afternoon

CRRRA Air Transport Brigade to Start Flying on New Year's Day: Two Aircraft to Arrive in Shanghai This Week

[Reported by this newspaper] The CRRRA Air Transport Brigade will start flying on New Year's Day next year, and two transport aircraft will arrive in Shanghai this week. The first flight is planned to transport the brigade's staff and materials to Guangzhou. The brigade's main station is located in Guangzhou. Currently, there are 111 tons of medical supplies in Guangzhou and 4 tons of medical supplies in Hankou, all of which urgently need to be transported to the interior.

According to the person in charge of the brigade: The brigade plans to fly two flights per aircraft per day in the future, estimating that each route can transport 12 tons of materials per day, 300 tons per month. From mid-January next year, it is hoped that each route can transport 1,000 tons per month. However, the CRRRA authorities, considering that air transport costs are very high, do not intend to transport large quantities, limiting it to urgently needed post-disaster relief materials and cases where there are no other transport tools available. According to the China National Aviation Corporation route, the air transport cost is much higher compared to water or road transport. For example, from Guangzhou to Guilin, air transport costs 383,000 yuan per ton, while water transport costs 131,797 yuan per ton. From Guangzhou via Guilin to Hankou, it costs 1 million yuan per ton, while rail transport costs 411,000 yuan per ton.

The Guangzhou director of the brigade is currently studying and will decide on the principles and work plan for transporting materials.

Sufficient Inventory, Hesitant Sales, Gradual Stability of the Rice Market, Yesterday Oil Prices Also Fell in a Straight Line

[Reported by this newspaper] Yesterday, the rice market was stable. A total of 3,230 dan arrived in the northern city, and 5,328 dan arrived in the southern city. In terms of prices: the southern city was negotiable, and the northern city only had a black market for slightly higher-quality cooked rice, initially at 67,000 yuan, then falling to 65,000 yuan. The reason for the black market was due to less goods arriving due to rain and rumors of ships pulling food. It was previously rumored that rice prices in the production area were higher than in this city, which is also true, but it is understood that the price increase in the production area was stimulated by the Shanghai rice market turmoil. If Shanghai rice prices are stable, it is not a concern. The relevant authorities estimate that the folk rice reserves in this city are at least 300,000 dan, and the rice that the municipal government can control, including that in Shanghai and en route, is almost no less than 2 million dan. With good allocation, it can supply this city for four or five months. The prospect of people's food is very optimistic.

The Banks of the Sichuan Gang Operate Stably and It Is Untrue That There Are Rumors of Instability

Recently, a leading figure in the Sichuan silver and money industry told reporters that it is not true that there are rumors of instability in the banks of the Sichuan Gang. The branches of the Sichuan banks in Shanghai have their annual loans allocated by the head office, so at the end of the year, only the loans need to be recovered and returned to the head office. Therefore, the silver roots of the branches are tight, but there is no phenomenon of capital turnover. The Sichuan Gang banks have always followed the old rules in their usual business operations and are quite normal. They rarely go beyond the scope of the legitimate business of banks. Therefore, in recent days, the amount of exchange has been doubled to prepare for any eventuality. The banks that are passively shaken on the Daily Report can not be included in the Sichuan Gang banks, because they are all newly established by foreigners who lived in Chongjin during the Anti-Japanese War. The outside world does not know the truth, and it is a pity to mix them up.

Person in Charge of China Textile Talks About Next Year's Production Policy

According to the person in charge of the China Textile Corporation, after the establishment of the China Textile Corporation, through continuous efforts, it now owns more than 2 million spindles, accounting for one-half of all spindles in the country. Among them, Shanghai is the center, accounting for more than 1.2 million spindles. Next is the Tianjin China Textile Corporation, with a total of seven factories, which were reorganized from 16 units of enemy and puppet textile factories, with a total of 320,000 spindles. The next is Qingdao, with 300,000 spindles. So far, about six-tenths of the total have started production. The China Textile Shanghai Company has a total of 19 textile printing and dyeing factories. Due to power restrictions, only more than 560,000 spindles have started production. The cotton production season is approaching, and the company has sent people to various cotton producing areas to purchase domestic cotton. It is estimated that the total amount of domestic cotton picked this season is about 5 million dan. Except for local needs, only about 1 million dan will flow to the market. The company's target for purchasing domestic cotton this period is 800,000 dan, but it is still not enough for half of the raw materials needed for production, so it still needs to use foreign exchange to purchase American cotton. It is reported that the steps of China Textile's production increase plan for next year are: (1) Self-purchase of generators. It is now actively installing four small turbine generators in China Textile's No. 16 factory, with a total power generation capacity of 4,000 kilowatts, which is only enough for the factory's electricity needs. In the future, it will continue to negotiate with the Executive Yuan Materials Supply Bureau to purchase generator installations. (2) Try to collect domestic cotton as much as possible to save foreign exchange and seek self-sufficiency in raw materials.

Resources Committee Takes Over Coal Mines and Obtains Loans of 1.5 Billion; Fuel Panic in the Jinghu Area Can Be Relieved

The board of directors of the Four Banks Joint Treasury recently resolved to lend 1.5 billion yuan to the Shandong Luda, Yuesheng, and Boda coal mines taken over and operated by the Resources Committee to alleviate the urgent needs of the mines for production. The entire assets of the mines are used as collateral, and the operating income of the mines is used as the repayment fund. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will each underwrite half, with a term of six months, and they are allowed to handle re-mortgages at a 30% discount with the Bank of China. It is reported that the scale of the mines is quite large, but the wartime damage was extremely heavy. After the Resources Committee took over, it plans to add a large number of equipment and materials, and the need for funds is urgent. Therefore, it borrowed a huge amount of money from the Four Banks Joint Treasury. The output of the mines can reach 50,000 tons of coal per month, which will be of great benefit to alleviating the fuel panic in the Jinghu area in the future.

Cotton Cloth Evaluation Council Decides That Cotton Cloth Prices Will Generally Increase by 10%

Cigarette Industry Faces Crisis; Costs and Tax Rates Are Too High; Important Meeting to Be Held

According to a person in charge of the Yizhong Cigarette Tobacco Factory in this city, after a large number of American cigarettes were imported into our country, the domestic tobacco industry has been in decline. Although the production and sales of domestic cigarettes are not as good as those of American cigarettes, the main reason is that the costs and tax rates are too high. Among the costs, labor is the largest, especially the year-end bonus issue, which makes major cigarette factories feel difficult. As for the tax rate, it has reached 100%, and the tax bureau also has plans to readjust it again. In order to solve the above difficulties, the Cigarette Industry Association has decided to hold an emergency meeting of all members at the association at 3:00 PM today to discuss a proper solution to the year-end bonus issue for workers, and said that many of the 86 cigarette factories in the city are unable to operate. There are more than 30,000 workers in the city's cigarette industry. The Cigarette Industry Association is constantly doing its best to overcome the current difficulties for the sake of itself and others, so as to avoid increasing worker unemployment. As for the tax issue, the association will send representatives Bao Gengsheng, Jin Yigeng, Shen Kunsan, Li Zitang, and Zhang Yuwen, etc., six people in total, to Beijing tomorrow to petition the Tax Administration, requesting a temporary exemption from adjusting the tax amount.

[Report from our correspondent in Nanjing on the 26th] Education is the foundation of construction. In the past, the percentage of education expenditure in the central budget estimates was very small, which was really unreasonable. Under the slogan of "Education First", education expenditure for next year is said to account for 5% of total national expenditure, which is a slight increase compared to 3.4% in the 34th year and 4% in the 35th year.

Border Education Conference Solemnly Opened Yesterday Morning

[Report from our correspondent in Nanjing on the 26th] The Border Education Conference convened by the Ministry of Education solemnly opened at 9:00 AM on the 26th in the Ministry's auditorium. Attendees included committee members Zhu Jiahua, Hang Liwu, Tian Peilin, Bai Zhentai, Ling Chunsheng, Max Wode, Aisha Yingxiang, Ma Hetian, Li Anzhai, Gu Jiegang, Han Rulin, and representatives from relevant agencies, totaling 67 people. Minister Zhu presided over the meeting, reported on the purpose of the meeting, and said that only three banners have been received in East Mongolia, border education has not been fully restored, and vocational education is still in its infancy. The Ministry will do its best to promote border education at all levels, and hope that colleagues will work together to promote progress. Director Ling of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Department reported on border education work and presented a report based on his observations and feelings. Committee member Bai Zhentai said that there is a lack of higher education in the border areas, and hoped to add colleges and universities and stipulate quotas for border education study abroad. Max Wode hoped to develop vocational education to meet the needs, improve the level of border education, and open up the knowledge of border people to avoid being confused by ignorance. Gu Jiegang said that to promote border education, it is necessary to start with social education. In the afternoon, more than 70 proposals will be divided into three groups for review. The first group is administrative expenses and treatment, convened by Bai Yunti to discuss with 18 people. The second group is school facilities, reviewed by Ma Hetian and 16 others. The third group is system courses, reviewed by Gu Jixun and 14 others. The review meeting will continue on the 17th.

International Cultural Cooperation Association Held a Founding Meeting in the Capital Yesterday

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 26th] The International Cultural Cooperation Association held a founding meeting at the Public Recreation Society at 2:00 PM on the 26th. More than 100 people including Shao Lizi, Peng Xuepei, Pan Gongzhan, Zhang Zhifan, Liang Hancao, and Hang Liwu attended. Zhang Daofan presided over the meeting and reported on the preparations. President Jiang's Instructions

To the participating members of the International Cultural Cooperation Association: Promoting international cultural exchange to enhance sympathy and mutual assistance, and to maintain the collective security of mankind, is the common belief of all nations in the world today. Our country's position is closely related to peace in the East and the world, and is extremely important and significant. Communicating culture should be regarded as a top priority. Your association's establishment today has profound meaning in the future history of culture. In the past 30 years, the world's academic thought and scientific inventions have made unprecedented and superior progress. We must catch up quickly without stopping, so as not to be left behind and compete in an aimless manner. China's traditional culture is long-standing, and the thoughts of saints and sages are broad and profound. The relics of ancient cultural relics are also extremely comprehensive and rich. We should promote and develop them to achieve the effect of pushing oneself and others to blend seamlessly. For the advantages of the cultures of various ethnic groups, we should select the strengths of all to use as a resource for correcting our own shortcomings. Only in this way can we merge the sources of Eastern and Western culture and make a powerful contribution to all mankind in the new era. Due to the high level of scientific development, the distance between ethnic groups is getting closer and closer, diplomatic relations are becoming more and more frequent, and cultural relations are becoming more and more close. How to seek harmony and cooperation, and weigh the similarities and differences, to enhance the friendly spirit among nations is the mission entrusted to all of you today. You are cultural pioneers, selected from the academic community, and your association is a new organization in our country's cultural world. You must have grand words and brilliant insights to fully exert your strength and promote world harmony through cultural power. I am offering these ideas at this grand meeting and hope that we can encourage each other.

Yesterday's Symposium in the City's Cultural and Educational Circles Discusses Textbook Issues; Renowned Educator Zheng Xiaocang Also Attends

[Our Newspaper's Report] Yesterday (the 26th) at 9 PM, the city's cultural and educational circles held a symposium at 851 Yuyuan Road to discuss textbook issues. Those who attended included Ou Yuanhuai, Shen Yougan, Zhang Yaoxiang, Huang Shijin, Chen Qingshi, Gu Shusen, Shen Baiying, Yu Qingtang, Gao Junshan, Chen Heqin, Zheng Xiaocang, Yang Zhixian, Zhang Yiqu, Fang Shannong, Sun Huaicong, Zhang Wenyu, Fu Tongxian, Liu Dajie, Dong Renjian, Liu Ganliang, Li Ximou, and Chen Weixiong, Yu Zhenying, a total of 23 people. First, Mr. Chen Heqin announced the outline of the symposium, the main aim of which was to discuss textbook issues. Then, Mr. Gu Shusen gave a report, stating: The nationally compiled textbooks originated before the war. The Ministry of Education only regarded them as a kind of standard textbook and did not call them "nationally compiled." "Nationally compiled" was actually a name given by the outside world. At that time, only the Chinese language textbook for senior elementary schools was printed and distributed in a limited way. When the War of Resistance broke out, the entire unified distribution method was planned according to national policy. During the war, seven publishing houses, namely Commercial Press, Zhonghua Book Company, Zhengzhong Book Company, Shijie Book Company, Datong Book Company, Kaiming Book Company, and Wentong Book Company, undertook the printing and distribution, each forming a "Seven-Publisher Alliance." After the victory, four publishing houses, namely Children's Publishing House, Culture Publishing House, Independent Publishing House, and Victory Publishing House, were added, which in fact had been opened up to an "Eleven-Publisher Alliance." The Ministry of Education, due to proposals from the Participatory Political Council, once advocated free opening, but due to various reasons, it is still carefully considering appropriate measures, and so on. Later, Mr. Chen Xiqin raised three questions: (1) Textbook editing issues: the advantages of nationally compiled and reviewed textbooks. (2) Textbook distribution issues: the importance of a free opening system versus the implementation of unified control. (3) Textbook content issues: a review of the current curriculum standards. Various experts expressed their opinions and discussions flourished until after 11 PM before dispersing.

Another dispatch: Last night, before the symposium, Mr. Chen Heqin hosted two banquets to welcome the renowned educator Mr. Zheng Xiaocang, who had just returned from the United States. During the banquet, he elaborated extensively on current university education issues. Mr. Zheng advocated that universities should not be run behind closed doors in the future, but should go outside the campus and connect with the public. His words were very insightful. After the banquet, Mr. Zheng attended the symposium to participate in the discussion of textbook issues.

Physical Education Performance Awards for Elementary and Middle Schools in Beijing

[Our Newspaper's Report from Nanjing] The Nanjing Municipal Education Bureau organized the city's first physical education performance for elementary and middle schools, aiming to promote all-around sports and focus on universal development. All public and private elementary and middle schools must select 20% of their total number of students to participate, in order to correct the past malpractice of "school sports only cultivating a few athletes." At the opening ceremony on December 4, Mayor Shen and Director Ma of the Education Bureau attended in person. Supervisor Hao Gengsheng of the Ministry of Education said, "This kind of sports performance is still a pioneering work in our country, and other places should follow suit in the future." A total of 60 schools, including 27 public and private middle schools and 33 public and private elementary schools, participated, with more than 6,000 students, holding a competition at the Central University sports field. There were more than 40 performances, and group competitions were divided into running, jumping, and throwing, held simultaneously. The situation was very enthusiastic, and the audience was huge. The roof of the Central University auditorium was also reached by the audience. The performances were of various forms, novel and moving. Eleven items were rated as A-level and thirteen items were rated as B-level in the middle school performances, and fourteen items were rated as A-level and twelve items were rated as B-level in the elementary school performances. Fifteen championships were set up for each of the male and female groups. The school with the most championships was Ginling Women's University Affiliated High School, with nine first places. 103 prizes were solicited in advance, and those who performed at A or B level were given certificates and prizes. The first place in each item of each grade in the competition was given a prize, and the remaining participants in the performance and competition were also given souvenirs as appropriate. The award ceremony was held at the Municipal Government Auditorium on the 23rd to encourage them. Twenty-six middle schools and thirty-three elementary schools won prizes.

Day 1 of Davis Cup Final: USA Wins Both Singles Matches Against Australia; Hurlburt Defeats Bromwich; Australian Star Suffers Unexpected Defeat

[Agence France-Presse, Melbourne, 26th] The Davis Cup final was held here today. The sky was cloudy and the weather was hot and humid. No less than 14,000 fans came to watch. At 1:30 PM, the players from the US and Australia entered the stadium. The band played the Australian and US national anthems. The President of the Australian Grass Court Tennis Association, Bullock, delivered a speech on the merits of Davis, the donor of the cup. The entire audience observed a minute of silence. The opening ceremony was completed and the competition continued. In the first group, Australia's Bromwich played against the US's Hurlburt. Bromwich was an Australian national player and the hope of winning was strong, but he was defeated unexpectedly. The score was 3-6, 6-1, 6-2, 0-6, 6-3. At the beginning of the match, Bromwich served first and was smooth, winning the first set in 23 minutes. Hurlburt came up in the second set and performed brilliantly. The last three sets became a battle of attrition. Both sides used long shots and never volleyed. In the second group, the US's Kramo played against Australia's Hean Choupears. Kramo was a better player and won 8-6, 6-2, 9-7. According to today's two sets of results, the Davis Cup has implicitly fallen into the hands of the United States, because Kramo's match against Choupears on the 28th will definitely be easily won. The United States has already won three of the five matches. Although the results of the remaining singles and doubles matches are difficult to predict, they are no longer relevant to the overall victory or defeat.

[Associated Press, Melbourne, 26th] The Davis Cup tennis final was held today on the tennis courts of the Old Eagle Sports Ground. The 14,500 seats in the sports ground were filled to capacity today, making it one of the days with the most spectators since the Davis Cup competition began.
