Administrative Briefs

Revised Measures for Thorough Investigation of Opium and Drugs; Administrative Affairs Office Notifies All Districts

The Civil Affairs Office convened a training session on opium prohibition laws for the directors of civil affairs sections in various districts on the 23rd of this month, explaining the opium prohibition laws and issuing "Shanghai Measures for the Thorough Investigation of Opium and Drugs." It is learned that Item 4 of the measures has been revised to: "This thorough investigation will be based on the affidavits provided by each head of household in the last investigation. The Bao Chief, Bao staff, and personnel dispatched by the police station will supervise the Jia Chiefs of each Jia to conduct a detailed investigation of each household under their jurisdiction. If anyone is found to be growing, transporting, selling, smoking, manufacturing, or hiding opium and drugs, or is suspected of smoking them, they will be immediately detained by the police station and dealt with according to law, and will be registered in detail according to the prescribed forms and reported to the municipal government for approval." It is reported that the Civil Affairs Office has notified all district offices.

Public Education Personnel Taking Exams Should Be Considered Official Leave

Examination Yuan Notifies Municipal Government

Regarding civil servants, school teachers and staff, and party affairs personnel, who request leave to take examinations, all should be considered official leave, retaining their original positions and receiving their original salaries. This was previously approved by the National Government for implementation. It is learned that the Examination Yuan Committee, under the order of the Examination Yuan, has forwarded the order of the National Government, that all civil servants of various agencies, school teachers and staff, and party affairs personnel who participate in national examinations according to law, or are selected, with valid proof, should be considered official leave, retaining their original positions and receiving their original salaries. All agencies are ordered to instruct their subordinates to strictly comply. It is reported that the Examination Yuan Committee has sent a letter to the municipal government to follow suit.

Private investment in road construction has truly opened up a precedent for municipal road administration.

District 4 (Penglai): Xia Yongsheng, deputy Bao Chief of the 19th Bao, resigned. Cai Boqian was elected to replace him. District 31 (Gaoqiao): Yang Xisan, deputy Bao Chief of the 21st Bao, should be re-elected due to a case. Huang Ruidai was elected to replace him by the Jia Chiefs of the Bao. In addition, Lu Shiwei, Bao Chief of the 5th Bao of the district, resigned due to illness. The Deputy Bao Chief was temporarily acting as Bao Chief. Xu Guoshan was elected to replace him by the Jia Chiefs of the Bao. Each district has reported to the city government for approval.

District 3 (Yu Temple): Zhang Youyin, Jia Chief of the 19th Jia of the 8th Bao, cannot take care of his work due to his busy schedule. A meeting of heads of households was convened and Zhang Youtao was elected to replace him. District 4 (Penglai): Liu Zhicheng, deputy Bao Chief of the 31st Bao, moved to another hometown. Mao Jianhua was elected to replace him by the Jia Chiefs. Each district office has reported to the city government for approval.

The 30th District People's Representative Assembly was held at 9 AM on the 23rd in the Workers' Union Hall of the Yizhong Tobacco Factory, 4 Lane, Peideli, Xiyangjiazhai. 23 resolutions were passed, and the representatives spoke very enthusiastically.

Page 9

A Record of Galloping Horses at Xin Suo Guan

— Special Dispatch from Xi'an, 8th Day of the Month; Correspondent Shao Shenzhi

I arrived in Yao County late at night. Although there were small shops outside the city, it was impossible to find lodging, and it was necessary to knock on the gate to enter the city. At this time, the sky was as black as ink, and you couldn't see your fingers. The desolate wilderness was silent at night, and only the barking of dogs echoed in the cold.

Yao County is built along the Qi River, with very high walls. To enter the city, one must cross the Qi River, and there is a gate on this side of the river. To knock on the gate, one must first knock on the gate of the outer defense. The so-called "blockhouse line" is only a little over ten li from the city. In Sanyuan in the morning, someone in the army told me: "When you get to Yao County, you may still hear gunfire. Just now there was a phone call saying that the Communists are attacking the line." Now that I have arrived at this "important place," it is already late at night, and I expect that the security will be extremely tight. Therefore, I devised a plan to "earn" my way through the gate. I draped a blanket over my shoulder and used a flashlight to explore the road ahead.

Earning Entry into Yao Gate at Night: The Gate Opens Under Red-Tasseled Spears

After walking for a while, I heard a loud challenge for the password in the darkness. I pointed my flashlight and saw a red-tasseled spear. It was a member of the local militia dressed in black. He stood across the gate, blocking my way. I explained where I was coming from and that I needed to enter the city immediately. The red-tasseled spear replied: "This gate is locked. Go look to the north." So I walked further north and encountered another red-tasseled spear. I thought that if this gate was also locked, I would have to find a way to get him to unlock it. Unexpectedly, the gate was ajar. I exchanged a few brief words with the red-tasseled spear. When he heard that I came from Sanyuan, he opened the gate without hesitation.

I crossed the Qi River on a flat stone bridge and went up a very steep, long slope. At the top of the long slope was the tightly closed city gate. After I knocked on the gate, a head appeared from the crack in the door and spoke to me. If I told him that I was a reporter from Shanghai, he would not understand and would not open the door. So I told him that I was from the local commissioner's office, returning to the city from Sanyuan with urgent official business. It seemed that the security was not as strict as I had imagined. While I was negotiating, two soldiers came up behind me. They took my place and spoke to the head in a commanding tone, ordering him to open the gate. The door gradually opened, and I saw that the head belonged to a soldier with a gun and ammunition.

We quickly entered the gate. There were no lights in the city, and it was as silent as death. Along the way, at street corners and alleys, we encountered many more red-tasseled spears. With the help of a soldier, I managed to get the door of a bathhouse-cum-hotel opened. The innkeeper was sleepy-eyed and made clicking noises between his teeth as he made my bed and brewed tea. Looking at the state of the inn, I understood the poverty of social life in Yao County, the so-called "gateway to northern Shaanxi." The water was salty, the bedding was black, and the brick bed was cold. Coupled with the snowy sky, the desolation was even more pronounced.

Generals Han Qi and Fan Zhongyan of the Song Dynasty once established their headquarters in Yan'an to defend against the three borders. The so-called "One Hundred and Twenty Qin Passes," of which Xin Suo, on the Cheng Yu road, was one of the most important passes. Defending the border outside the One Hundred and Twenty Qin Passes was a life of distant garrison service. When the situation became unfavorable, Fan Zhongyan established his headquarters in Yao County, which was then called Yao Prefecture. "Old Fan's belly is full of tens of thousands of soldiers," and the people of Yao County greatly admired Fan Zhongyan. The current county government is located where he had his headquarters. The place where this famous general of the western frontier held court and inspected his troops still exists, now with a plaque that reads "Jing Fan Tang," and serves as the county government's courthouse. The courtyard is narrow, with an old cypress tree. The light is dim, and it faces the drum tower in the center of the city, just a hundred paces away.

It gives people a sense of the border city's military atmosphere of the past, and one can almost hear the sounds of metal weapons and galloping horses.

However, Yao County is in Guanzhong, not the border city of the Han and Tang dynasties. But in the Eastern Han dynasty, there were also Western Qiang, and the entire Guanzhong region was a border area. From hinterland to border city, times have changed, and thousands of years have passed unnoticed. Outside the city, the Qi and Ju rivers flow gently, telling of the vicissitudes of life. It has always been "far" from Chang'an. Although it is now connected by railway, transportation is still difficult. The people of Yao County still look back to the past, believing in myths and legends.

(Top) Inside Yao County (Bottom) Drum Tower in Front of Jing Fan Tang (Photos by Special Correspondent Shao Shenzhi) A Panoramic View of Tongguan Coal Mine (Photos by Special Correspondent Shao Shenzhi) Slogans Seen in the Wilderness of Northern Shaanxi (Photos by Special Correspondent Shao Shenzhi)

City of Myths

Yao County also has a stele forest, a private collection of over sixty stone tablets, housed in a solitary, dark, and lightless building that feels like a cave. Most of them are Northern Wei votive inscriptions, with strange and unrestrained brushstrokes. Unlike the Longmen Grottoes votive inscriptions, there are few elegant and graceful pieces. However, there are two extremely complete Thousand Buddha steles. This cannot be compared with the scale of Yungang or Dunhuang, but the carvings are neat and detailed. Thousands of identical Buddha statues in relief equally illustrate the depth and surging tide of Buddhist culture. In addition, there are several Sixth Dynasty stone Buddhas with broken legs and feet. There are also a dozen or so tattered Republic of China army infantrymen who look like beggars. Some of them, like the Sixth Dynasty stone Buddhas, sit under the wall in front of the solitary building, watching the red-tasseled spears drilling on the large parade ground, chanting "one, two, three, four." Others pile up some dead branches and yellow leaves next to the Wei steles, burning them for warmth, the smoke stinging the eyes, nose, and throat. I squeezed into this small house that had become a smoke-filled cave, and with tears in my eyes, I finished looking at the strangely styled steles and stone Buddhas. The group of living stone Buddhas stood up and said to me:

"What should we do? Officer." I didn't know what to do either. After talking with them, they all began to chatter incessantly. They said that they were originally from the 22nd Army, stationed in Toutoulin, but were captured because "the Eighth Route Army attacked us." "The Eighth Route Army had so many men! How could we not be defeated?" I said that Xi'an had sent troops to rescue them, right? "That was after we were defeated that they came to rescue us!" They said, "The Eighth Route Army said to us: What are you fighting for? You fight, and then they come to rescue you. If you want to join the Eighth Route Army, you can stay here. If you don't want to, we'll send you back. We don't want to join. They fed us well on the way here, but when we got here, the county government only gave us two *cang* a day per person. How can we get enough to eat? They don't even believe us when we sigh. It's cold!"

So that's how it was. No wonder they were asking this "officer" what to do. They were wearing suspicion like clothing and given two *cang*, unsure whether it was relief or punishment. I asked around for them in this small city, but couldn't find a solution. The general trend made me understand that the solution had already been decided, which was to do nothing and let nature take its course.

The people of Yao County believe that they live in the middle of a boat. The Northwest lacks water, and they imagine that the place where they live is a boat. They have reason to say so: Look, there is a Ju River and a Qi River, and the county seat is like a boat floating in the middle. They don't know in what year, but a well was dug in the county government office, and the boat started leaking. Yao County was flooded. Later, they quickly filled it in, and cast a half iron bull to stabilize the boat, so that we could live peacefully. I did see a half iron bull. This has more practical significance than Noah's Ark in the Old Testament. They also boast of the Tang Dynasty calligrapher Liu Gongquan and the Sui Dynasty scholar Sun Simiao, the "King of Medicine" whom the people of northern Shaanxi piously worship. The Liu family north of the city was originally the ancestral home of Liu Gongquan, so this place name has been preserved from the Tang Dynasty to the present.

North of Sanyuan, the terrain rises continuously. From a distance, it looks like a mountain, but when you climb to the top, it is a plain. When you look at the outer mountain from a distance, you see a plain again when you climb up. It has a bold and imposing aura. This is the characteristic of the Qin-Long Loess Plateau. The place names in this area are all "something-yuan." The widespread use of the character "yuan" originated in Qinzhong. South of Chang'an is Leyouyuan, which in ancient Chinese literature represents beautiful scenery. But the "yuan" here is a village, farmland, the so-called edge of the Guanzhong Plain area. The Jinghui Canal area is uniquely blessed, and cotton can be harvested at a world record of 120 catties per mu, while here it is only twenty or thirty catties, a stark contrast, but still enough for a general standard. The soil is thin, and the water conservancy is insufficient, relying on the heavens for harvest. There is a saying in Qinzhong: "Eighty-three months of rain," meaning that there is hope for a harvest if it rains in the third, eighth, and thirteenth months of each year. This saying is especially applicable to the arid areas north of Yao County.

These days the blockhouse line is tense. When I arrived, I didn't hear any gunfire, but the commissioner and county magistrate shouted that it was terrible. Gu Zhutong, the commander-in-chief of the army, told them clearly when he came to Xi'an last time: "If you lose the county government, defend the office; if you lose the office, defend the desk." This is the responsibility of the county magistrate. The inspection at the city gate is particularly strict.

A broken county town, the streets are also covered with horse and mule droppings, to allow it to dry easily, because severe winter is about to descend. There is a mountain east of the city named "Mount Wutai" to adorn the faith of the people of Yao County. Even more beautifully decorated is the Medicine King Temple, with its gold and jade splendor. A large cart road leads directly to the county seat, and the incense burns year-round. Middle school students in the county seat kneel before the mud statues, shaking medicine containers, to seek prescriptions for someone in their family. Sun Simiao was undoubtedly a good doctor in the Tang Dynasty. According to the inscribed record in Lingjing, Emperor Taizong of Tang once visited Sun and asked him to serve as an official, but Sun still lived in seclusion here. He praised him, saying, "If he does not become one of the three dukes, he will surely become a famous doctor." He conferred upon him the title of "True Man." Sun wrote the "Essential Formulas Worth a Thousand Gold," and Guo Si, a scholar of the Song Dynasty Huiyou Pavilion, had it engraved in Huazhou to spread it widely. Later, another set was engraved in the Taoist temple. Now these stone steles are as complete as ever, because there are not many rubbings, and the inscriptions are clear, all of which are simple prescriptions. The "Overseas Formula" stele contains Sun's notes on his pillow and health preservation inscriptions, which are mostly in line with scientific principles. The main idea is quiet health preservation, revealing traces of the confluence of Confucian and Taoist thought. The backwardness of culture shows the strength of the power of gods and ghosts. The people of Yao County bring wine to the mountains to worship such temple gods, and their images shine. Myths circulate, while life is poor. If anyone were to try to close it down, they would undoubtedly be strongly opposed. Some people believe that it is better to be immersed in superstition than to be awakened. Moreover, they do not know when they will be saved again.

Wheat Fields on the Loess Plateau: Public and Private Wastelands for Anyone to Cultivate

The Xian-Tong branch line ends at Yao County. There are coal trucks from Yao County to the coal mine at Wulipu, five miles south of Tongguan, which also sell passenger tickets. From Wulipu to Tongguan Jin Suo Guan, you must hire a horse-drawn carriage.

On the loess plateau in this area, galloping on horseback, pulling on the reins, and looking at the boundless world, the rise of the northwest has been liberated from the labels of closed and backward since the development of the interior from the coast.

On the road north from Yao County to Jin Suo Guan, the wheat is green, but there is still so much wasteland. The government encourages land reclamation, but after a while, only the slogan remains: "Public and private wastelands, for anyone to cultivate." It is not very effective, because land reclamation requires capital and labor, and promoting a new movement requires organization. Over the years, the main theme of the county governments has been handling military service, maintaining the old methods of production. Tongguan County alone has built two hundred blockhouses, while the county's population is only 56,000. Yao County has only 50,000 people, Sanyuan has less than 100,000, and Yijun has less than 40,000, all of whom have a frightening burden.

A highway roughly follows the Qi River northward, with mountains on both sides. Where the loess has eroded, the Permian limestone layer is exposed, as well as conglomerate and shale. The wheat fields I saw were on both sides of the Qi River. Horses and mules run in the fields and eat the wheat, and no one thinks it strange, but people from the south would find it strange. At this time, farmers do not want it to rain or get warmer, otherwise the wheat will grow taller, and it will be difficult to have a good harvest next year, because the soil is loose and they are afraid that it will not be strong. They even need to flatten it, so these wheat plants are like piles of wild vegetables, flat and spread out in the field. At this time, they do not mind the trampling and grazing of sudden horses, as long as it grows firmly. There is a farmer's saying here: "Pigs in the first month, cats in the second month, women running all over the ground in the third month." In the first month, the crops have not yet sprouted, so pigs are allowed to run wild. In the second month, cats are in heat and do not stay home. In the third month, farm women pick wild vegetables everywhere. This is the case throughout the northern wheat belt.

All along the way, there were farmers driving mules. Some were transporting coal from the Jin Suo Guan area to Yao County, and some were carrying corn to the city to sell. But there were no mule carts, the only tool for travel, which shows that there was no travel. The ancient road was desolate. The horse I was riding was borrowed from the army, but it was not thin. Walking with these farmers, I felt that the men were thin and the warhorse was fat. They drove their mules, shouting loudly, or cursing intimately, with the whip cracking, making the ancient road a little less lonely. Their shouts were only short commands, mostly with one sound, occasionally with a retroflex sound. They said that there were more than a hundred commands for driving mules, which could not be recorded in writing or phonetic symbols. They could use commands to control the speed and direction, but when I learned their commands, I couldn't control the mules. They said, "The mules recognize the sound." The mules are all raised very fat. They say, "Four fish mixed with feed are better than bait." This saying means that as long as the grass is mixed evenly, the livestock will eat it all, without special bait.

They rely on pitiful agriculture, and the agricultural knowledge and life accumulated by the gods and ancestors. There are often many moving farming songs buried in the Chinese countryside, and this place is no exception. They sing of the weeds, saying, "Artemisia capillaris in the first month, artemisia annua in the second month, cut down and burned as firewood in the third month." They say that the tender grass in the first month is as fragrant as artemisia capillaris, and praise artemisia capillaris (a medicinal herb that can be soaked in wine). The grass is green in the second month, and the grass is lush after the third month, ready to be used as fuel. This is also the season when the ground is frozen and the grass is yellow. As I listened, I actually wrote down a large pile of proverbs. I felt that due to the difference in latitude, water conservancy, geology, and climate, their expectations for rain and early harvests, or their predictions of the weather, were significantly different from those in the south.

They have their own names for animals and plants. Male pigs and dogs are called "tooth pig" and "tooth dog," while females are called "grass pig" and "grass dog." Cats are called "lang cat" and "female cat." However, male horses are called "son horse," and female horses are called "mule horse." Male mules are called "son mule," and females are called "grass mule." Middle-aged pigs have a special name, they call them "Kalangzi." Crickets are called "vinegar spiders," and ants are called "butt floating horse." These are all local dialects. Artemisia capillaris is called wild flat bean, and Bupleurum chinense is called chicken tongue. They hate cuckoos, calling them "murdering robbers," because their calls are unpleasant and they have no good feelings for them. They do not know the elegant names given to this bird by scholars and poets.

Flocks of wild pigeons and wild chickens gather in the wheat fields, flying slowly and in large numbers. If there were hunting guns, there would be a harvest.

Tongguan Coal Mine

Last year on Double Tenth Day, Tongguan County was renamed Tongchuan County. When people in Shaanxi talk about Tongguan, they specifically call it Northern Tongguan, because the pronunciation is the same as Tongguan. The telegraph bureau's Latin alphabet spelling encountered difficulties and often sent the telegrams of the two counties to the wrong place. But Tongguan Coal Mine is still Tongguan Coal Mine.

There is a severe coal shortage in Xi'an, but tens of thousands of tons of coal have accumulated in Yao County and Tongchuan, with mixed coal selling for four or five yuan per ton. The price in Xi'an is three times higher. Some employees on the Cheng-Tong branch line have given up their jobs waving red and green flags to traffic in coal, making a profit of three times their salary. I asked why the Longhai Railway could not transport the coal to Xi'an to alleviate the coal shortage this winter. The answer was that there were not enough cars. At present, the average daily output of Tongguan Mine is 650 tons, and the Longhai Railway's demand is 600 tons. That small difference is pulled out. However, of the investment in Tongguan Coal Mine, the Longhai Railway accounts for two-thirds and the provincial government accounts for one-third. According to the share capital calculation, the provincial government said that it should be given 200 tons. Coal merchants have great ability and can find ways to transport some coal out, because the interest on the Longhai Railway is disguised as selling carriages. Along the way, car inspectors, switchmen, and even staff members extort money. Everyone at the station has great power. A switchman said that if he doesn't throw the switch, the car won't start. Transportation is also full of difficulties. The Longhai Railway's fault is that coal prices in Xi'an are so absurdly high. Therefore, there are mule teams and hand-pushed carts transporting coal on the Xian-Yu highway. There are twenty-some private small mines in Tongguan County. These hawkers only choose large pieces because they are easy to transport. Small pieces or broken coal are piled up in the mine, and no one asks about them. The Longhai Railway has a Longhai Enterprise Company. The Japanese invaded Northeast China's South Manchuria Railway, with the railway as the center, developing enterprises and doing big business. People in Shaanxi asked what enterprises the Longhai Railway has. Running the road well is enough. I heard that they recently registered with the authorities.

When I arrived at the Tongguan Coal Mine in Wulipu, the new and old mine directors were in the process of handing over the work. The mine director is determined by the council formed by the provincial government and the railway bureau. The new mine director, Ma Qingyuan, is an old member of the Tongmenghui. From the era of the Shaanxi Jingguo Army to the extension of the central government's power into Shaanxi, his army entered Xi'an and he served as the first garrison commander, and has always taken a firm attitude against Yang Hucheng. Before the victory, he was a consultant to the Military Affairs Commission. He retired this year and received a pension. "Without this pension, I wouldn't even be able to travel," this 54-year-old veteran said to me with a firm attitude. "Tongguan Coal Mine has made contributions during the War of Resistance, and it is the only large coal mine in the Northwest. We must take a long-term view and operate this mine from the standpoint of developing the Northwest." When it comes to coal quality, it cannot be compared with Guanyintang in Henan, let alone Jiaozuo. It contains 5% sulfur and is semi-anthracite coal. He said, "If transportation becomes smooth in the future and the output of other mines becomes more flexible, this mine will have problems." However, he believes that standing on the standpoint of developing the Northwest, we will never dislike opening another mine. "And we can find ways to reduce costs and make the selling price lower."

There are more than 6,000 workers in this mine. The average wage per worker is only about 1,600 yuan, and the monthly salary of an engineer is only about 200,000 yuan. The treatment is low and should be improved immediately. The Longhai Railway takes 600 tons of coal and only charges the cost plus 20% profit. However, the Longhai Railway delays payment and does not allow itself to sell coal. The Longhai Railway's losses are compensated by the coal mine. So he sighed and said to me, "I've only been here for eight days, and I don't know the internal situation very well. I always feel that this problem is very serious. There are many personnel problems. Now the first thing to do is to adjust the treatment. The shortcoming of state-owned enterprises is that there are too many office staff, and sometimes their treatment is higher than that of engineers. This is also an unreasonable phenomenon here. I have already told everyone that I am definitely not here to make money at the mine. If I take improper wealth, please report me."

Currently, there are four plants, twelve shafts, and several abandoned shafts. Three shafts are contracted to merchants, and about seven are in operation. The power is a few abandoned locomotives. The materials and machines are pieced together during the war. If we increase equipment, it is impossible to do so. If it is done, the output will naturally increase, but the transportation problem cannot be solved, so there is still no talk of development. The workers all live in cave dwellings, which are warm. There are mosquitoes in December. The hospital at the mine has a record of diagnosing 7,800 cases of malaria and other infections last year. This means that on average, everyone has seen a doctor once. The second most common is eye disease, followed by respiratory diseases. There are thousands of diagnoses for each.

The area of the mining area is more than 2,600 hectares, and the estimated reserves are 50 million tons. The entire Tongguan coal deposit belongs to the Carboniferous-Permian coal-bearing system. The large anticline limestone that runs from east to west divides it into northern and southern regions. After prospecting, the coal wells mined by local methods have penetrated the coal-bearing system and reached the limestone. Observing with columnar section diagrams, the northern coal seam dips northwest, high in the east and low in the west, low in the south and high in the north. The average thickness can reach four meters, with a total area of 44.7 million square meters. Taking the specific gravity as 1.3, the total reserves are 284.44 million metric tons. If only half of it is minable, then at a daily output of 4,000 metric tons, it can be mined for a hundred years. However, at present, including more than 20 private small mines, the daily output is only 1,200 metric tons.

I ran to the No. 1 well, which is more than 60 meters deep. There is no methane, and oil lamps can be lit. This well is mined using the room-and-pillar method. The mining slots have developed an area of 700-800 mu. Water is drained in the natural pores of the limestone. The Tongguan rock layer has more soft shale and less hard shale, so only the room-and-pillar method can be used. The miners wear thick cloth on their heads, with oil lamps tied to their foreheads, flames dancing. They push carts or drag coal baskets, crawling like earthworms. This is also life. They work eight or twelve hours, rotating shifts. The privately operated local method of mining requires workers to switch shifts every ten days and a month. During the shift change, they eat and sleep at the bottom of the well, without seeing the sun, truly underground workers.

Shape of Jin Suo Guan Graphic by the Newsroom of this Newspaper

Good Cave Dwellings Seen in Northern Shaanxi Have Sufficient Air and Light (Photos by Special Correspondent Shao Shenzhi)

The Strategic Importance of a Mighty Pass: A Panoramic View Southwards Towards Chang'an

From Tongguan to Huayin within the Guanzhong Basin, is what's known as the Jing and Wei plains. Its geography is similar to that between Beijing and Shanghai, yet its width is only tens of miles, and its area is only 40,000 square miles. (In my article "Guanzhong Covered with Frost and Snow," I described the irrigation projects of the Shaanxi Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau. Besides those, there are several canals that the Shaanxi Provincial Agricultural Improvement Institute assists in constructing: the Wugong Weihui Canal irrigates 2,000 acres; the Yunyang Yinhong Canal irrigates 20,000 acres. This canal uses dams to divert mountain floods for irrigation. The mountain floods bring with them a high concentration of phosphorus fertilizer. The Weinan Huohui Canal irrigates 20,000 acres, built using funds from the British China Relief Fund and will be completed this winter; the Fuping Fuhui Canal irrigates 20,000 acres, and will be able to release water next spring. These are the major irrigation projects in Shaanxi.) From Sanyuan to Yaoxian, after dozens of miles, you reach the edge of the plain. Climbing a mountain, I saw a vast plain. This is actually a loess plateau. Reaching Tongguan, you enter the mountains, and it becomes even higher at Yijun, forming the spine separating northern Shaanxi from Guanzhong. In Yijun, even in summer, one needs to wear a lined jacket. Emperor Wu of the Han dynasty once built the Yuhua Palace here as a summer retreat. North of Yijun towards Huangling and Luochuan, the terrain becomes lower again. The Jinshuo Pass, located between Yijun and Tongguan, stands majestically in the mountains like a natural barrier, becoming an important strategic point since ancient times, which is no accident.

The Guanzhong Plain is high in the west and low in the east, leaning against the Liupan Mountains in the northwest and separated by the Ziwu Ridge in the north. The northern Shaanxi region, north of Tongguan and Yijun, is also a basin, leaning against the Ziwu Ridge, high in the west and low in the east, covered with loess and red soil, making it a good wheat-growing area. Northern Shaanxi is isolated, and the people are poor, but the land is not barren, which is quite different from common perceptions. Since the Qin and Han dynasties, it has been abandoned to the Western Qiang people. Throughout history, whenever there were troubles in the west, it was always considered a strategic location for warfare. Zuo Zongtang pacified the Hui rebellion, and his subordinate Liu Songshan marched north from Xi'an to Suide. After the Republic of China was established, there was the so-called "banditry" in the region. Li Zicheng rose from northern Shaanxi, needless to say. Consequently, water conservancy was neglected, education was stagnant, the imperial court considered it a border area, and officials regarded it as a perilous route. Guanzhong and northern Shaanxi, though geographically close, felt like a thousand miles apart. Despite having fertile land, there was no development. This is the case for most of the Northwest, not just a corner of northern Shaanxi. Looking at the situation in the Jinghui Canal area after water conservancy was improved, and then riding a horse in front of the Jinshuo Pass, the barren mountains are severely eroded, with crisscrossing gullies. Hillsides that could be good farmland are now all wasteland. The court and public are engaged in lofty discussions and political debates, while conflicts continue. On the lines of blockhouses, opium is rampant. The further north you go, the cheaper it becomes. The decline of the people's livelihood is evident.

The terrain in the areas the reporter traveled through is extremely complex, making detailed surveying very difficult. The Ziwu Ridge meanders to Yijun and Tongguan. At first glance, it is all loess, but in the southeastern area of Tongguan, there is a large area of exposed red soil, which is likely the famous Sanmen Series red soil. The loess layer originally covered the red soil and can be dozens of meters thick, indicating severe erosion. The reason why the He Plateau looks like hills from afar is due to erosion and fragmentation. Often, two plains are separated by a deep valley, making it impossible to pass through, requiring a long detour, and the valley floor becomes a road or wheat field. A few hours of heavy rain can create a gully. Although the loess is thousands of feet high and seems stable, the degree to which it can be eroded is highly concerning.

The county seat of Tongguan has only two thousand and some hundred residents. Traveling thirty miles north, you arrive at the Jinshuo Pass. Going west from the pass, it is only a dozen or twenty miles to Guanqian. The reporter originally planned to go north to Huangling, but the roads were often blocked at this time, and incidents frequently occurred. After a ten-day trip through seven counties, it was possible to get a glimpse of the local conditions, so I turned back to Xi'an. The Jinshuo Pass was built during the Song dynasty. During the Qing dynasty, for defense purposes, there was only one garrison officer stationed there, later changed to one sergeant, with twenty soldiers. Each soldier received silver for only eight months each year, at one tael per month, and five piculs of rice per year, supplied by the county. The locals can still talk about it, showing the difference in burdens between now and then. Now, the reporter rides a horse in front of the pass and sees only a stretch of the pass wall, descending along the mountain. Two mountains converge, and the rocky cliffs create a dangerous path. The old pass entrance has been widened into a highway heading north. The function of the "mighty pass" of the past has completely disappeared. Climbing the pass and looking around, the vastness stretches in all directions. Looking south, from a high vantage point, everything is visible. The remains of the border pass include former barracks and reclaimed land, with half-withered willows, resembling an old veteran with a gray beard, hoeing and farming at the foot of the mountain, gazing at the setting sun over the Southern Mountains.

Hygiene and Medicine Published every Friday

A Brief Discussion on the Uses of Plasma

— Yi Jianlong

Significant progress has been made in therapeutic drugs during the Second World War. This remarkable progress has provided a deeper level of protection for human health and lives. In terms of the order of progress, the first can be said to be the synthesis and evolution of mineral preparations; the second is the preservation and unlimited use of plasma; and the third is the invention and mass production of penicillin. People in the country clearly have a considerable understanding of the therapeutic value of the first and third, while the uses and methods of the second seem to be only partially understood, and even abandoned altogether due to improper use. In the early years of the War of Resistance, the author studied blood transfusion therapy with experts in the United States and Canada, and later presided over a blood bank in Kunming for many years. Based on research and experience, I will give a brief introduction.

(1) Composition—To know the uses of plasma, one must first understand its effective components. Plasma is made from unclotted blood and is a mixture of colloidal and crystalline substances. Its effective components can be described as follows:

(A) Essential Nutrients—All nutrients that have been digested by the gastrointestinal tract must be absorbed and transported through the plasma before they can reach the tissues of various parts of the human body. Furthermore, the remaining or stored nutrients in the tissues must also be absorbed and transported through the plasma before they can enter nutrient-poor tissues. From this perspective, plasma is nothing less than a general hub for nutrients. All nutrients needed by the human body, such as proteins, amino acids, fats, fatty acids, glucose, vitamins, and inorganic salts, are readily available.

(B) Substances Maintaining Osmotic Pressure—The circulating blood volume in a healthy human body is constant, accounting for 9% of body mass. Its ability to remain constant depends largely on the osmotic pressure within the plasma. This osmotic pressure can prevent the exudation of fluid from blood vessels, and can also return what has already exuded back into the blood vessels. There are two substances in the blood that maintain osmotic pressure: proteins and salts.

(C) Endocrine Hormones—Endocrine hormones are the mechanisms that constantly regulate changes in various parts of the human body. For example, thyroid and growth hormones control development, insulin controls carbohydrate metabolism, and ovarian hormones control fertility. These endocrine hormones originate in endocrine glands and are transported to various organs through the blood. Therefore, endocrine hormones are also present in plasma.

(D) Various Enzymes—Metabolism and detoxification in the human body are mostly mediated by enzymes. The plasma contains a variety of enzymes, the most important of which is thrombin.

(E) Various Antibodies—When the human body is invaded by bacteria, it produces antibodies that circulate in the plasma to fight the bacteria. The types and amounts of antibodies in the blood vary from person to person. In most mixed plasma, the types and amounts of antibodies are generally higher.

(F) Other Life-sustaining Factors of Unknown Origin.

(2) Uses and Methods—Knowing the effective components of plasma allows us to infer its uses. The uses and methods of plasma can be described as follows:

(A) Traumatic and Surgical Shock

The etiology of shock is still under debate, but its significant pathological change, the escape of plasma from blood vessels, is generally recognized. Due to the action of certain malignant factors, the blood vessels dilate and permeability increases, causing plasma to escape into the surrounding tissues. As a result, the circulating blood volume is greatly reduced, and the supply of oxygen and other nutrients to the tissues is insufficient. If not treated immediately, the patient will likely die within nine to twelve hours. The effective method for treating shock is the rapid infusion of plasma. American shock expert Dr. Scudder said, "If blood is not transfused when it should be, death is imminent; insufficient blood transfusion is a waste of effort." Blood specific gravity, hematocrit, and blood pressure are the three standards for determining the timing and quantity of blood transfusion. If the blood specific gravity and hematocrit are higher than normal, while the blood pressure drops to below 70%, it is clear evidence that the blood is too concentrated and the heart's pumping volume is greatly reduced, and a large amount of plasma should be infused immediately until all three return to normal. The expressions of shock patients in our country are often not as obvious as those of Caucasians. Even when facing life-threatening situations, they remain calm, so laboratory tests and diagnosis are very important. If the patient can still eat and has no symptoms of dehydration, concentrated plasma or concentrated serum albumin can be injected intravenously to increase the osmotic pressure within the blood vessels, so that the plasma that has permeated into the surrounding tissues returns to the blood vessels. To prevent the occurrence of surgical shock, it is best to infuse 300 to 500 cc of plasma before and after major surgery. This procedure has become an indispensable routine in operating rooms of major hospitals in the United States.

(B) Hemorrhagic Shock

Bleeding from internal and external injuries can cause shock, but massive hemoptysis, gastrointestinal bleeding, ectopic pregnancy bleeding, and metrorrhagia can also cause severe shock. The difference between this type of shock and the shock mentioned above is that blood specific gravity, hematocrit, and blood pressure all decrease simultaneously. In this situation, plasma should be infused rapidly through multiple veins simultaneously to help the patient survive the critical period, followed by the infusion of whole blood or red blood cells. If the circulating blood volume is lost by more than one-third, it can be life-threatening, while the loss of red blood cells, if it does not exceed 60%, can still maintain its minimum level of gas exchange.

(C) Burns or Scalds

Severe burns or scalds can cause shock. Therefore, in addition to local treatment, plasma should be infused to prevent shock. Even after the shock has passed, plasma continues to leak from the affected area. According to Dr. Scudder's estimate, if a third-degree burn covers one-third of the body's surface area, the amount of plasma lost from the affected area in 24 hours is more than 4000 cc. To maintain the patient's normal blood volume, plasma infusion is essential. If the patient can still drink, concentrated plasma should be used.

(D) Secondary Anemia

The treatment for this type of anemia is to eliminate its source and promote the production of red blood cells. To promote the production of red blood cells, it is necessary to supply as much of the raw materials for red blood cell production as possible, including proteins and iron. Plasma contains sufficient protein and other nutrients, which can supply some of the raw materials for red blood cell production, so it can be an adjunct to iron therapy.

(E) Malnutrition

In severe malnutrition, the protein in the blood is lower than normal. As a result, water continues to permeate from the blood into the surrounding tissues, forming systemic edema. For this type of patient, only by measuring the protein in the blood and continuously injecting concentrated plasma can the patient recover quickly.

(F) Protein Deficiency Syndrome

Protein deficiency syndrome is caused by fatty changes in the renal tubules. In these patients, blood protein is continuously excreted from the kidneys. As a result, the protein in the blood is significantly reduced, and systemic edema can also form. These patients should also be treated with plasma. If the daily excretion of protein is more than 25 grams, and the patient cannot consume more protein, then 400 cc of plasma should be infused daily, since the protein content in plasma is usually around 7%.

(G) Febrile Diseases

In patients with diseases such as typhoid fever, typhus, and tuberculosis, gastrointestinal digestion and absorption are abnormal, and the body's consumption is high, resulting in a negative nitrogen balance. This pathological change not only reduces the patient's resistance but can also cause adverse complications. If plasma is continuously injected in addition to drinking more fluids, it can increase the patient's nutrition and resistance.

(H) Gastrointestinal Diseases

Whether or not these patients have undergone surgical treatment, if they cannot consume more nutrients, their condition will inevitably deteriorate. The remedy is to continuously inject plasma to increase nutrition and promote the healing of the affected area. An immobile adult needs at least 50 grams of protein per day, which requires 700 cc of plasma. Healthy plasma contains 7 grams of protein per 100 cc.

(I) Acute Infectious Diseases

Mixed human plasma contains a variety of antibodies, so it is effective against measles, pertussis, chickenpox, scarlet fever, erysipelas, and adenitis. American pediatrician Dr. Bavenberg's experiments have proven that among 4,733 children who received measles prevention injections (20 to 40 cc of plasma injected intramuscularly per person), only six cases of primary measles were found, while among 11,280 children who did not receive measles prevention injections, 94 developed primary measles.

(J) Premature Infants

With the advancement of modern medicine, infants born less than six months after conception can also be kept alive. In addition to regulating the temperature of the incubator, providing oxygen, and special nutrition, small amounts of plasma can also be continuously injected.

(K) Increased Intracranial Pressure and Breast Lumps

For these patients, continuous injection of concentrated plasma or concentrated serum albumin while reducing fluid intake is much more effective than treatment with magnesium sulfate laxatives.

Although plasma has many uses, there are also contraindications. In cases of organ dysfunction, excessive blood pressure, congestive heart failure, or acute pulmonary edema, plasma infusion should be used with caution, and large amounts are especially not recommended.

(3) Methods for Distinguishing the Quality of Plasma—After the victory of the War of Resistance, surplus dry plasma from the US military also flowed into our country's market along with other surplus materials. The modern pharmacopeia does not yet have methods for distinguishing between good and bad products. However, it is inevitable that the quality of various products will vary. To facilitate identification, I will briefly describe the dry plasma identification method for users' reference:

(A) Color—Expired dry plasma is a light, amorphous powder that is always straw yellow. It should not be used if it is clotted or has a light green tint.

(B) Unexpired dry plasma should dissolve completely within one minute after adding distilled water.

(C) Solution Turbidity—Turbidity is a common physical property of liquid plasma, but under an photoelectric colorimeter, its turbidity should not exceed 700 degrees.

(D) Residual Moisture—The residual moisture in dry plasma should not exceed 1.0%.

(E) No Pyrogens—Pyrogens are the corpses or waste products of bacteria. If the equipment used to prepare the plasma is not washed with special chemicals, or the soda water used to dissolve the dry plasma is not disinfected with a special filter, then a fever reaction is unavoidable.

Protein Hydrolysates: Their Physiological Effects and Therapeutic Efficacy

— Lecture by Xu Zhaodui, Recorded by Tao Shouqi

In-depth research on protein nutrition began more than forty years ago. At that time, famous scholars made contributions to the understanding of the protein content of food, the conversion rates of protein and nitrogen, the body's nitrogen balance, and the biological value of proteins. Later research also clarified the analysis of amino acids, the identification of essential amino acids, the relationship between proteins and edema, and so on. However, previous work was largely scattered and unsystematic. Chittenden's research concluded that the human body's need for and tolerance of protein was quite low, which had a somewhat dangerous impact, because the general public was under the impression that the protein needed by the human body was very easy to meet. At that time, research on vitamins was developing rapidly and soon showed its importance. As a result, general clinicians today only pay attention to vitamins and often neglect the importance of proteins. It was not until recently, due to the application of novel and rapid protein detection methods, and the mass production and therapeutic development of protein hydrolysates, that the topic of protein nutrition has once again aroused the interest and attention of the medical community.

Main Functions of Proteins The main functions of proteins in the human body are briefly described as follows:

(1) Maintaining Blood Volume—The urgent function of proteins The proteins in plasma are a colloidal substance, so they can produce an effective osmotic pressure to resist capillary blood pressure, preventing excessive leakage of fluid from the blood vessels, and maintaining blood volume. Any injury is often accompanied by the exudation of plasma proteins in addition to bleeding, which reduces the osmotic pressure of the blood and thus aggravates the reduction of blood volume.

(2) Maintaining the Integrity of Tissues The results of research on bedsores have shown the importance of proteins for tissue integrity. Patients with bedsores have low protein levels in the blood and a negative nitrogen balance. If their protein intake can be increased, causing the nitrogen balance to become positive, then the bedsores will also heal, because tissues lacking protein nutrition have reduced vitality and are prone to collapse.

(3) Promoting Wound Healing A lack of protein affects the growth of fibrous tissue, making it difficult for any wound to contract. Postoperative wounds often tend to rupture when the protein in the plasma is too low. If protein intake can be increased, the wound will heal quickly.

(4) Promoting the Production of Immune Bodies, Endocrine Hormones, and Enzymes The existence of this function is only a hypothesis and needs to be clearly confirmed before it can be established.

(5) Functions During Recovery The protein metabolism during the recovery period from illness often undergoes significant changes due to the following factors: A. Patients who experience loss of appetite, nausea, or vomiting during illness may reduce their protein intake. B. The diet in hospitals often contains too little protein due to economic or other difficulties. C. Patients with gastrointestinal disorders have poor protein absorption. D. The impact of exudation—Any loss of fluid from the body is accompanied by a loss of protein, especially the fluid exuded from burned surfaces or large abscesses, which contains a particularly high mass of proteins. Therefore, patients with large-area burns or empyema often lose no less than fifty to sixty grams of protein per day. E. The amount of protein excreted in the urine during illness or injury is often several times higher than normal. From the above five points, it can be seen that the human body during illness or injury is often deprived of large amounts of protein. Therefore, it is necessary to supplement protein during the recovery period.

Highly Nutritious Therapy The daily nitrogen content in a typical natural diet is about 10 grams, while in a high-protein diet it is 20 grams. Therefore, if the need for protein increases to a considerable extent in a diseased state, it is by no means something that a natural diet can cope with, and amino acids or protein hydrolysates must be given. When the need for protein intake exceeds the amount that natural food can supply, it is called hyperalimentation.

Application of Protein Hydrolysates Pure amino acid mixtures (Translator's note: Amino acids are the final product that protein becomes when it is digested or broken down, and they are absorbed by the gastrointestinal tract. Their relationship to protein is like glucose's relationship to carbohydrates) are difficult to manufacture and expensive, so protein hydrolysates are more suitable. Protein hydrolysates can be manufactured from milk, meat, fish, soybeans, brewer's yeast, or other protein-containing foods. The application of protein hydrolysates has the following advantages: (1) It does not require digestion. (2) The volume is small. (3) It can be taken as a medicine, unaffected by appetite. (4) It avoids conflicts with hospital authorities who want to save on patients' food expenses. Its main disadvantages are: (1) The taste is not good. (2) It can cause diarrhea when taken in large amounts.

Therapeutic Uses of Protein Hydrolysates

(1) Peptic Ulcers The hyperalimentation therapy for peptic ulcers has already been discussed by Dr. Xue Bangqi in a previous article in this column, so there is no need to repeat it here.

(2) Malnutrition In patients with malnutrition, treatment with hyperalimentation therapy can cause edema to subside and blood protein and red blood cell levels to return to normal within four to five days.

(3) Pulmonary Tuberculosis The combined use of hyperalimentation therapy and other treatments for pulmonary tuberculosis can accelerate the improvement of the condition.

(4) Postoperative Care The use of hyperalimentation therapy after surgery, especially gastrointestinal surgery, can promote the patient's nutrition and shorten their recovery period.

New Medical Talks

Latest Vitamins

— Shao

Although folic acid has been discovered for many years, its chemical structure was only elucidated and its artificial synthesis successfully achieved most recently.

Chemically speaking, folic acid is composed of the following three different chemical groups: pterin, p-aminobenzoic acid, and glutamic acid. Pterin is a type of yellow pigment found in butterfly wings; folic acid is also a yellow crystal.

Folic acid was originally a component of the vitamin B complex, initially called the "Lactobacillus casei factor" because it is an essential nutrient for the growth of *Lactobacillus casei*. Recent reports indicate that folic acid is also an essential element for human hematopoiesis and has specific effects on various megaloblastic anemias, similar to liver extracts. However, liver extracts are difficult to purify, and their determination requires clinical cases of pernicious anemia, resulting in high prices and inconvenient application. Folic acid is an artificial synthetic product that does not require biological determination. With mass production in the future, the price will inevitably be low, and the day when it completely replaces liver extracts is not far off.

As early as 1935, Day et al. reported that natural folic acid (initially called Vitamin M) had the effect of preventing a nutritional anemia in white mice. However, the therapeutic effect of this artificial synthetic product on human megaloblastic anemia was not discovered until 1945 by the American vitamin expert Spies et al. Spies et al. tested it on several cases of nutritional megaloblastic anemia common in the southern United States and obtained the same therapeutic effect as liver extracts, namely a rapid increase in the number of reticulocytes in the blood, followed by a steady rise in the number of red blood cells and hemoglobin levels. This year, it was also tested on Sprue, megaloblastic anemia during pregnancy, and true pernicious anemia, all with similar success. These results have been fully confirmed by Darby, Moore et al., and Zuclzer & Cgden et al. in the same country. Recently, Wilkinson et al. in the United Kingdom used folic acid in five cases of pernicious anemia and also obtained equally satisfactory results.

However, folic acid is not the active ingredient (antianemic factor) in liver extracts. Folic acid is a bright orange-yellow crystal, while the most refined liver extracts are colorless. Willmson believed that folic acid might stimulate the production of blood factors in the liver. However, according to the experimental report published in the October issue of the Journal of Pathology and Bacteriology last year by Jacobson & William in the United Kingdom, the antianemic factor in the liver and folic acid may belong to the same class of compounds, and their main chemical group is pterin. According to the research of these two scholars, synthetic xanthopterin and leucopterin, as well as liver extracts, can all produce the same reticulocyte response in splenectomized rabbits, while other substances such as iron and various vitamins (unfortunately, folic acid was not tested) do not have this effect. Therefore, they believe that the liver antianemic factor may be a pterin derivative.

World Health Organization (Continued)

— Qiao Shumin

1. A New Definition of Health: The preamble to the organization's constitution first sets forth the most progressive and broad definition of health, considering health to be a state of complete physical, mental, and social well-being, not merely the absence of disease. It also recognizes that the highest attainable standard of health is a fundamental right of every human being, regardless of race, religion, political belief, economic, or social status. Furthermore, it believes that governments have an inescapable responsibility to protect the health of their people. Readers, consider: What is the view of the Chinese people regarding the meaning of health? How many people enjoy this fundamental right? Has the government fulfilled its responsibility to protect the health of the people?

2. Regarding the Function of Hygiene: They all believe that scientific hygiene studies can greatly contribute to peaceful coexistence among human beings in this turbulent world. They firmly believe that sanitary facilities will raise the living standards of the people and promote the economic prosperity of society, thus assisting in the accomplishment of our common goal—world peace. They all believe that only a healthy and well-nourished people can truly understand the true meaning of basic freedom. They also believe that public health is the active and comprehensive crystallization of many scientific principles. In many advanced countries, thanks to sanitary facilities, the average lifespan of the people has doubled compared to the previous century. However, the development situation in various countries is very uneven. In some countries, hardly half of the children born can live to the age of five, and the average lifespan of their people is only half that of the people in more developed countries. They also believe that to achieve the great purpose of the World Health Organization, we need the greatest and most sustained efforts of our hygiene medical personnel. However, our efforts alone will not be enough. We must mobilize all of humanity so that they can understand the principles of hygiene and fight together. Readers, consider: How many of our people understand the true meaning of basic freedom? What is the average lifespan of our people? Only heaven knows, perhaps only half that of the United States and Britain. To what extent are our hygiene medical personnel working hard? To what extent are the people mobilized?

3. Regarding the Impact of Unhygienic Conditions: They all believe that in the field of hygiene, countries are interdependent and interconnected. Epidemics in any region can endanger other countries. Low standards of health among the people not only hinder the economic prosperity of their own country but also affect the overall prosperity of the entire world. Readers, consider: What is the impact on our country and the world of the annual epidemics of smallpox, cholera, typhoid, dysentery, relapsing fever, measles, kala-azar, plague, hookworm disease, schistosomiasis, tuberculosis, and so on?

4. Regarding the Future Mission of the World Health Organization: In the future, all previously established international health organizations will be merged into this new World Health Organization. It will use all the latest scientific knowledge and equipment to conquer diseases and plagues. Therefore, epidemic prevention remains the primary task. However, this is only the first step. One must know how many people in the world are struggling below the starvation line! Therefore, using our nutritional knowledge to cooperate with efforts in agriculture and food production to achieve freedom from hunger is also one of the goals. The second step is to positively and actively promote physical and mental health to achieve a higher level of physical development, a longer lifespan, more effective productivity, and a more meaningful life.

However, if humans cannot coexist peacefully and there is another major war, then everything will be destroyed together, and hygiene will be in vain. We should know that science can be used for good or for evil. The key lies not in the scientists themselves, but in the awareness and conscience of the broad masses of people to determine the good or bad fortune, life or death of human destiny. From the standpoint of striving for world peace, the World Health Organization seems to be a gathering point for uniting people from all over the world, a place for friendship among people with different cultures and beliefs, and may perhaps become a stepping stone for a world peace organization. I cannot help but offer my sincere wishes!

Peptic Ulcers Diagnosed by X-rays

— Chen Youxin

There are two significant differences between X-ray examinations of the stomach and X-ray examinations of the lungs. The first is the difference in tissue structure. The lungs can naturally show their outline under X-rays without relying on an additional medium. This natural revelation is impossible for the stomach, so a special medicine is usually needed to fill its interior to be examined. This medicine is either pure barium sulfate or barium sulfate synthesized with other non-essential ingredients. Taking this medicine alone has a limewater-like appearance and a soil-like taste. This medicine is very good; it does not cause any chemical reactions in the gastrointestinal tract, does not interfere with the work of the gastrointestinal tract, does not cause any side effects, and is not toxic, but it can help with the examination. The second difference is that the work of the stomach is intermittent, while the work of the lungs is continuous. In this way, the examination of the stomach needs a starting point and an ending point. The starting point is to start the examination when the stomach is empty, and the ending point is when there is no residue of barium in the stomach. Between these two points, the examination can be adjusted according to the actual situation. From this point of view, the stomach examination is more complicated compared to the lung examination.

The method of examining the stomach is equally important for fluoroscopy and radiography. In terms of the diagnostic value itself, fluoroscopy is more important than radiography. During fluoroscopy, the position of the stomach can be freely changed, any part can be palpated, any suspicious area can be observed in detail, the tenderness can be measured, the softness or stiffness of the stomach wall, adhesion or protrusion, or the hyperactivity or decline of stomach function, the freedom or discontinuity of peristalsis, and the muscle contraction or relaxation of the pylorus or any part can all be obtained with a correct concept. Of course, the shadows of the lesion itself can also be revealed on the fluoroscopic screen at the same time. However, radiography also has special effects. This is not only a record of the shadow that can be used for later reference or as a blueprint for consultation, but it can also provide information that was missed or not clearly displayed during fluoroscopy.

If the above methods cannot be summarized into an accurate diagnosis, then there are several special examination methods that can be used. I will skip over them briefly for now. There is also a situation where the symptoms of the stomach occur as a result of diseases in other parts or systems. For example, many so-called indigestion or stomach pain are caused by diseases of the cecum. There are also so-called true stomach wall erosions that are caused by brain problems. But even for diseases of the stomach itself, X-ray examination cannot necessarily lead to a definite conclusion. However, most of the failures are mostly due to the mildness of the disease and the short duration of the illness. There are also cases where the presence of many secondary signs buries the main signs of the disease during X-ray examination. Therefore, in many cases, the results of X-ray examination can only be regarded as a clinical reference, like other laboratory methods, and cannot be regarded as a diagnosis. However, if the result is very clear, or if the examiner is very experienced and confident, then this is equivalent to a perfect and independent diagnosis.

Some people also suspect whether the amount of X-rays received during a stomach examination will have any harm to the body? This answer can be negated based on modern knowledge. The amount of X-rays that commonly causes at least a minimal biological change is difficult to exceed in a thorough stomach examination, which means that this kind of consideration is superfluous under normal circumstances.

Now I want to talk about why patients with peptic ulcers need X-ray examinations. First, of course, to check if an ulcer exists. If it is confirmed, then its location, size, depth, and number need to be clarified. Secondly, it is necessary to measure its connection with stomach function, digestive obstruction, pyloric obstruction, stomach wall adhesion, or anything else. Second, to distinguish whether this ulcer belongs to the ordinary category or the so-called malignant category. Third, it is about the selection of treatment methods. Even during the treatment process of the ulcer, X-ray re-examination is also necessary. Determining the effectiveness of the treatment, this kind of re-examination is very helpful. Furthermore, after using surgical operations, the examination of the stomach not only provides powerful reference in clinical methods, but can also take timely measures to prevent the recurrence of ulcers.

Regarding the X-ray signs of ulcers, the most definitive and valuable is the "niche" sign. The "niche" shadow is an organ with a disease that has a small protruding area on its outline. This is the shadow caused by the ulcer itself being filled with the medicine. The location of this "niche" is mostly on the upper edge of the stomach or at the tip of the duodenum that directly communicates with the stomach, occasionally on the pylorus or the lower end of the esophagus. Although stomach ulcers themselves are far fewer in number than duodenal ulcers, the "niche" itself is relatively easy to find in the stomach. However, it is not easy for every ulcer patient to show this important sign, so sometimes it is necessary to rely on other signs to confirm the diagnosis. I will omit the details for now.

Now I will talk about when a stomach examination cannot be performed. Sometimes, a stomach examination is inappropriate or should be delayed. For example, after stomach bleeding, palpation during the examination may cause renewed bleeding. There are also times when the ulcer is about to perforate, then the surgery during the examination may also cause adverse consequences.
